WNW Advisors · deliberation atlas

Ten rounds, twelve personas, thirty-six decisions.

A drillable map of the ten-round, twelve-persona deliberation behind the WNW strategy. The spine shows how aligned the room was each round; the rail below shows the six tensions that threaded several rounds and closed at integration. Click any round to open its weave, then click any node to jump to that exact point in the transcript.

ICP and segmentation

opening positions strongest case each, then the concession
P1 SaaS Buyer
Most founders don't care about OSFI. Don't narrow me into a closet.
concession the subset I'm describing as "narrow" — SaaS firms that do sell into banks — is exactly the subset with the least price sensitivity and the clearest WTP, because for them SOC 2/dual-regime…

concession my motion is slow, association-gated (FS-ISAC, ABA/ICBA/CCUA — R04 §E) and capacity-heavy (R05). And understanding the vendor's world genuinely helps a TPRM engagement — so the bridge is real…

read in transcript →

Trust flows one direction — regulated proof down to SaaS, never up.
concession regulated trust is the slowest and hardest to earn, and a firm may need SaaS cash flow to fund the climb to it. That is a real sequencing constraint — but it's a funding argument for SaaS, not an…

frame the room converged on first: Separate the originating engine from the converting asset
contested D21–D24
convened P5 GTM & Demand Lead P9 Partnerships & Ecosystem Builder P3 Boutique Operator P1 SaaS Buyer P2 Regulated Buyer
opening positions strongest case each, then the concession
P5 GTM & Demand Lead
Borrowed pipeline buys the first year; the OWNED expertise engine is the only thing that makes the next ten clients repeatable. Build it from day one or you rent your pipeline forever.
concession the owned engine is slow to compound — it front-loads senior hours and converts on a lag (R04 B: receptiveness is High but content-to-conversion is a Medium inference, not a measured rate). In…
read in transcript →
P9 Partnerships & Ecosystem Builder
You can't out-publish your way to the first year, and worse — you can't even SEE the bridge trigger without a partner sitting at it. Borrowed pipeline isn't the faster path; for our wedge it's the ONLY path to the trigger in time.
concession borrowed pipeline has a tax I won't hide. It is not owned — the partner can reprice, change programs, or build the capability in-house (the GRC-platform double edge from R02: Vanta/Drata partner…
read in transcript →
P3 Boutique Operator
Every one of these channels spends the SAME scarce hours — the founders'. The motion isn't 'pick a channel,' it's 'which channels originate WITHOUT stealing the founders' delivery time,' because in year one selling time IS delivery time.
read in transcript →
P1 SaaS Buyer
I move fast and I buy digitally. I'll find you when my deal stalls — IF you're findable and you have a finish-lined offer I can say yes to that afternoon. Don't make me sit through a relationship-building cycle when I have a contract waiting.
read in transcript →
P2 Regulated Buyer
I will not be rushed, and I should not be. I buy on documented proof, peer endorsement, and a face I've seen at my association — none of which you can accelerate with a content blitz. Earn my channel; you can't buy it.
read in transcript →

Carried tension · how it traveled

Smallness fork (is the wedge big enough)

P12open by design

P12 keeps asking the existential question: is the cross-border, both-sides bridge actually big enough to feed a boutique, or is it a sliver that starves the firm before the slow bank motion matures. The room's answer is that the model is supply-bound, not demand-bound, so the whole bet turns on one unmeasured number: whether the wedge fills two or more senior calendars at a premium.

R2
Round 2 · Demand and timing thesis
P12 frames the fork at the demand round: there is no verified demand for one cross-border both-sides firm. It enters the ledger as trigger T1.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
R3
Round 3 · Competitive landscape and white space
The 'empty for a reason' challenge: maybe the white space is vacant because it cannot be held, not because nobody noticed it.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
R6
Round 6 · Pricing and economics
The economics round tests it: does the pricing survive at achievable volume? P11 finds a knife-edge and the fork stays open.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
R7
Round 7 · GTM motion and channels
Named outright as the plan's load-bearing trigger: does the GTM motion generate enough qualified volume to fill the senior books?
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
how it closed

Converted to the load-bearing instrument; open by design. See the reconciliation in Round 10 →

Carried tension · how it traveled

Owned vs borrowed origination

P5 / P9reconciled in principle

P5 wants the owned, expertise-led origination engine built from day one so the firm is not renting its pipeline forever. P9 counters that for this wedge you cannot even see the bridge trigger without a partner sitting at it, so borrowed pipeline is not the faster path, it is the only path to the trigger in time. The fight is about the mix, not either-or.

Carried tension · how it traveled

Channel pace vs regulated anchor

P1 / P2reconciled by frame

P1, the SaaS buyer, moves fast and buys digitally the moment a deal stalls. P2, the regulated buyer, refuses to be rushed and buys on documented proof and peer endorsement. The tension is a pace mismatch, plus the need to keep the firm's visible identity anchored on the regulated side without that costume slowing the SaaS deal.

Round 7 · GTM motion and channels
Resolved structurally into a two-channel split: a fast digital SaaS channel and a slow, association-gated bank channel.

Carried tension · how it traveled

Founder-time vs capacity floor

P3 / P11reconciled by structure

P3, the boutique operator, holds the founder-time veto: every channel and every service line spends the same scarce senior hours, and it cannot all be the founders. P11, the unit-economics modeler, holds the capacity floor: the per-advisor economics and the senior-hour ceiling are the binding constraint the whole plan sits on. This is the supply-bound reality of a senior-led boutique, and it is the thread most directly about whether the founder can actually staff the business.

R5
Round 5 · Service design and packaging
Service design forces the question: who delivers each line item, and at what utilization? P3's veto lands and P11 sets the economic floor the catalog must clear.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
R6
Round 6 · Pricing and economics
Pricing makes it concrete: the fixed fee divided by the senior hours has to clear the specialist band after the pod takes its share, or the premium is a story, not a price.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
R9
Round 9 · Execution architecture
Execution makes it structural: every milestone declares its senior-hour cost, Phase 1 must fit the founder's post-delivery hours, and a quarterly capacity gate gets a real veto on which ladder rungs the firm climbs.
go to this point in the transcript →open the round weave
how it closed

Reconciled by structure (D29 / D31 / D32). See the reconciliation in Round 10 →

Carried tension · how it traveled

Canada timing

P7reconciled by sequence

P7, the regulatory authority, argues that the freshest principles-based supervision right now is Canadian, with the OSFI Streamlined Framework live as of June 2026, so Canada should not be deferred behind US association seals. The tension is about timing and sequencing the two regimes rather than a contradiction.

Double-edged smallness

R03the moat-side face of the fork

The same smallness that looks like a vulnerability in the first tension is also the moat. A niche narrow enough to worry P12 is also one that neither the platforms below nor the Big-4 above can cheaply cross, and it is cheaper to own mindshare in. This thread is the optimistic face of the smallness question.

round: 1 title: ICP and segmentation date: 2026-06-27 moderator: Moderator (neutral chair) personas_convened: P1 SaaS Buyer · P2 Regulated Buyer · P6 Competitive & Market Analyst · P10 Trust & Buyer-Psychology Expert · P12 Strategic Skeptic inputs: research/01-market-sizing.md · research/02-competitive-whitespace.md · research/03-pricing-value.md · research/04-channel-acquisition.md · research/05-capacity-economics.md (via STATE summary) · research/00-source-brief.md (segments/triggers/regulatory bridge) decisions: ICP definition(s) · segmentation · trigger map status: complete defect_logged: no

Round 1 — ICP and segmentation

The question on the table

WNW targets two very different buyers — Series A–C software companies and small/mid banks & credit unions — across two countries (US/FFIEC and Canada/OSFI). Round 1 must decide: is this one ICP or two; how narrowly is each drawn; where do the motions converge and where must they split; and what fires a buy. It must do so against the live, double-grounded tension the gate handed forward: P12's "pick ONE segment / one country / one motion and dominate," now backed by both a demand argument (R02: demand for a single cross-border both-sides firm is unverified) and a capacity argument (R05: senior dual-regime hours are the scarce binding resource — four quadrants may be unstaffable).

Sequencing (which motion leads, US vs Canada timing) is explicitly Round 2's decision, not this round's. Round 1 defines the ICPs and the segmentation and hands the beachhead choice forward with the evidence needed to make it.

The pivot the room kept returning to: the regulatory bridge

Before the persona positions, one piece of evidence reframed the whole round, so it is recorded up front. The brief documents — at Primary/High confidence (regulator guidance) — that the two segments are two ends of one regulated transaction, not two unrelated markets:

  • A bank/FRFI is accountable for its third parties by rule: US joint FDIC/Fed/OCC community-bank guidance and OSFI B-10 (third-party) + E-21 (operational resilience) make vendor oversight a full-lifecycle obligation. [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build] (brief [S28][S34]).
  • That obligation cascades to the vendor: "if you supply technology to a bank, B-13 is effectively your problem too." [Opinion (regulator-paraphrase) · Primary · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S36]). B-10 contracts name specific clauses — audit rights, ~30-day termination, breach notification, fourth-party oversight — that a SaaS vendor must satisfy to close the deal. [Fact · Primary · High · Supporting · Build] (brief [S34]).
  • OSFI's Streamlined Framework (launched 25 June 2026) literally moves buyers across the bridge — letting provincial credit unions continue federally and fintechs ("innovators") become federally regulated deposit-takers. [Fact · Primary · High · Supporting · Build] (brief [S15]).

This is what makes R02's "intersection" defensible rather than coincidental. "We serve both SaaS and banks" is me-too (R02 §B: Echelon, IS Partners, Compass IT already do it). "We sit on both ends of the same FFIEC+OSFI vendor-diligence relationship and speak both regimes" is the vacancy R02 found empty (R02 §F). P6 advanced this; P12 attacked it; the Moderator records it as the spine of the round, gated on demand.

Persona positions (strongest case each; argument, not assertion)

P1 — The SaaS Buyer: "Most founders don't care about OSFI. Don't narrow me into a closet."

The SaaS job-to-be-done is singular and urgent: unblock the deal or the round. SOC 2 becomes pressing the moment the first six-figure enterprise/bank deal hits the pipeline and procurement sends a security questionnaire — typically ~Series A, $1–2M ARR, budget but no in-house security leader. [Fact · multi-source · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S17][S18]). The founder is buying outcome and speed, not a program, and resists open-ended retainers (per my charter).

My objection to the room's "bridge" enthusiasm: the bridge is real but it describes a minority of Series A–C SaaS. The median founder selling to other software companies neither knows nor cares what B-13 is. If you define the SaaS ICP as "only those selling into regulated FIs, cross-border," you have just deleted most of a ~10–11K-company eligible pool (R01 §B) down to a sliver you haven't sized. That is how a boutique starves before its slow bank motion matures.

Concession (after the bank/competitive case): the subset I'm describing as "narrow" — SaaS firms that do sell into banks — is exactly the subset with the least price sensitivity and the clearest WTP, because for them SOC 2/dual-regime readiness is the gate on a contract worth far more than the fee (the deal-unblocked value metric, R03 §B). So I'll accept a core-and-perimeter structure: narrow core for margin and positioning, broader perimeter for volume — provided the perimeter isn't abandoned.

P2 — The Regulated Buyer: "The bank won't care that you also do startup SOC 2. That can read as a liability."

My job is defensibility in front of an examiner and comfort in front of the board — survive supervision, avoid an MRA / enforcement / AMP (Canada: $10K–500K CAD, brief [S35]), and not be the institution in the breach headline. I refuse startup-speed talk and anyone who can't tell B-13 from B-10. [charter]

The strongest evidence for my primacy: my segment has the only independently measured WTP in the whole research set. Across ten years of CSBS data, the smallest community banks spend 50–64% of their consulting budget on compliance (vs 19–30% at the largest); consumer compliance alone is ~38% of advisory spend. [Fact · Major · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R03 §D; CSBS 2015–2024). That is a structural, recurring budget line — not a hypothesis. And the value I pay for is examiner-survivable judgment, which R02 §E shows is precisely the layer platforms and AI cannot automate. The FDIC even cautions us to avoid "costly and unnecessary" consultants [Opinion · Primary · Medium · Supporting] (R03 §D) — which means I pay only for defensibility, never for commodity hours. That filters out exactly the competitors who can't go deep.

My objection: "we serve both software companies and banks" doesn't earn my trust — it spends it. If WNW reads as a startup shop dabbling in banking, I won't put it in front of my examiner. The cross-border (OSFI+FFIEC) fluency, on the other hand, is genuinely scarce and genuinely valuable — that's the part I'd pay a premium for.

Concession: my motion is slow, association-gated (FS-ISAC, ABA/ICBA/CCUA — R04 §E) and capacity-heavy (R05). And understanding the vendor's world genuinely helps a TPRM engagement — so the bridge is real value to me, as long as the firm's identity is anchored on the regulated side.

P6 — The Competitive & Market Analyst: "The bridge is the only thing that makes 'both-sides' non-me-too."

Map check. Both-sides alone is occupied — at least Echelon, IS Partners, Compass IT already straddle SaaS SOC 2 and US bank FFIEC work. [Fact · Vendor/firm · Medium · Critical] (R02 §B). Cross-border (FFIEC+OSFI) at the boutique tier is thin — US boutiques are FFIEC-only, Canadian boutiques OSFI-only, only Big-4 span both (at enterprise price). [Fact · Vendor/firm · Medium · Critical] (R02 §C). The intersection — both-sides AND cross-border at boutique tier — surfaced nowhere. [Synthesis · Medium · Critical] (R02 §F).

So the ICP must be drawn toward the intersection, and the bridge (S36) is what makes the intersection a coherent buyer story instead of "a firm that happens to do two things." The defensible ICP isn't "all SaaS + all banks" — it's the subset of each segment that sits on the same vendor-diligence relationship: SaaS vendors selling into regulated FIs (especially cross-border), and the FIs managing them under FFIEC + OSFI.

Structural warning that should drive the ICP narrowing, not just color it: the SaaS commodity layer is where compression is fiercest — Vanta/Drata partner programs and Cynomi-class AI vCISO platforms ($37M Series B, ~2× throughput per human) are eating evidence-collection, control-mapping, and baseline reporting. [Fact · Medium · Critical] (R02 §D/§E). A SaaS-volume play runs straight into that grinder. The examiner-defensibility / dual-regime-judgment layer is the durable one. Anchor the firm's identity on the defensible axis even if you land volume elsewhere.

P10 — The Trust & Buyer-Psychology Expert: "Trust flows one direction — regulated proof down to SaaS, never up."

Trust is the core asset in this category, not a marketing afterthought (per my charter; the brief's own defensibility thesis). The decisive asymmetry for the ICP: regulated/examiner-survived proof transfers down into SaaS credibility, but SaaS SOC 2 proof does not transfer up into a CRO's trust. "We keep banks defensible under FFIEC and OSFI" is a credibility flex to a founder selling into banks. "We do startup SOC 2" earns nothing from a Chief Risk Officer about to put us in front of an examiner.

The implication for segmentation: the firm's master credibility narrative must be anchored on the regulated side — examiner-survived references, regulated-shop proof, dual-regime depth — because that is the proof that compounds and travels. The SaaS motion can borrow that trust; the reverse is not available.

Concession: regulated trust is the slowest and hardest to earn, and a firm may need SaaS cash flow to fund the climb to it. That is a real sequencing constraint — but it's a funding argument for SaaS, not an identity argument. Don't confuse the two.

P12 — The Strategic Skeptic: the last challenge (steelman of the opposite)

I'll steelman three alternatives the room is gliding past.

  1. Pick ONE and dominate. The intersection ICP is elegant on a slide. But you have zero buyer evidence that anyone wants one firm for both regimes and both sides — it is a Critical×Low trigger in two files (R02 #2; R03 #1). And R05 says the binding resource is senior dual-regime FFIEC+OSFI hours, a web-unmeasured sliver of talent. A core that requires four quadrants (SaaS/bank × US/CA) staffed by people who barely exist is not a strategy, it's a hiring fantasy. What would have to be true for the intersection ICP to be right? (a) the bridge-subset is large enough to feed a boutique, and (b) you can staff dual-regime delivery. Neither is established.

  2. Pick a different ICP. Maybe the real ICP is only the bridge subset — SaaS-selling-to-banks — and standalone community banks are a distraction. Or maybe it's only US community banks, and Canada/OSFI is bolted on for a differentiation story you can't yet staff or sell.

  3. Do nothing yet on the cross-border axis until one buyer pays for it.

I'm not vetoing the bridge — P6 and the regulator evidence make it the most intellectually honest spine available. I'm insisting the decision be written as gated, not as a finding. The intersection is a hypothesis with a beautiful regulatory rationale and no demonstrated demand.

Forced disagreement → reconciliation (Skeptic gets the last word before each decision)

The room did not converge cheaply. P1 wanted breadth (volume/pipeline), P2 and P10 wanted a regulated anchor (depth/trust), P6 wanted the intersection (defensibility), and P12 wanted one beachhead and a gate. The reconciliation that survived every challenge:

  • Not one blended ICP. The two buyers, jobs, cycles, channels, and WTP bases are genuinely different (R01–R04). Merging them produces the generic "we do security for everyone" position R02 calls me-too. Rejected.
  • Not two unrelated ICPs run in parallel. R05's capacity finding kills four simultaneous quadrants; R02 says both-sides-as-coincidence is occupied. Rejected.
  • Two distinct ICPs, joined by the documented bridge, drawn toward the intersection, with a core and a perimeter — and the beachhead/sequencing decision explicitly deferred to Round 2 under the capacity bound. This is the only structure that holds the wedge (R02), respects capacity (R05), keeps P1's volume concern alive (perimeter), and survives P12 (everything load-bearing is gated). Adopted, provisionally, with triggers.

P12's last challenge before recording: "You're defining an ICP on a buyer demand you have never observed." Acknowledged and built in — every Critical claim below that rests on the intersection demand, the bridge-subset size, SaaS WTP, or dual-regime staffing carries a VALIDATION TRIGGER. The ICP definition stands as the provisional working target, not a proven market.

DECISIONS

D1 — Two ICPs, bridged, not merged; identity anchored on the regulated side

WNW serves two distinct ICPs that are two ends of one regulated vendor-diligence relationship. The structural reason one boutique credibly serves both is the regulatory bridge (brief [S28][S34][S36]) plus dual-regime (FFIEC+OSFI) fluency — not convenience. The firm's master credibility narrative is anchored on the regulated side (P10's one-directional trust flow), and the SaaS motion borrows that trust. - Rests on: bridge mechanism [Primary · High · Build] (brief S28/S34/S36); intersection vacancy [Medium · Build provisionally] (R02 §F); trust asymmetry [Opinion/P10 · argument]. - Gated on: T1 — demand for one cross-border both-sides firm [Critical × Low · VALIDATION TRIGGER] (R02 #2; R03 #1). The ICP is the working target; commitment to the intersection awaits the buyer probe.

D2 — Narrow each ICP toward the bridge: a defended core, a leveraged perimeter

Each segment is drawn as a core (toward the bridge — high WTP, defensible, priced above commodity) and a perimeter (general work — volume/cash, served with leverage, never with scarce senior hours).

SaaS ICP - Core: Series A–C software companies (~$1–2M ARR+, budget but no in-house security leader) whose buyers/roadmap include regulated FIs and/or who operate cross-border US+Canada — the subset facing dual-regime vendor diligence, with the clearest WTP and lowest price-sensitivity (P1's concession; deal-unblocked value, R03 §B). - Perimeter: general Series A–C SOC 2/ISO readiness buyers — real volume (~10–11K eligible stock, R01 §B) but commoditizing (R02 §D/E). Serve via productized/platform-leveraged delivery (R05 leverage option), not senior judgment hours.

Bank ICP - Core: small/mid banks & credit unions (US/FFIEC + Canada/OSFI) with active third-party / fintech-risk programs, especially those with cross-border exposure or on the OSFI Streamlined-Framework path (brief [S15] — the literal vendor→bank crossover). Examiner-defensibility value metric (R03 §B/§D). - Perimeter: general small/mid FI cyber / exam-prep work, single-regime. - Why narrow toward the bridge: it is what makes the position defensible (R02 §F), priced above the compressing commodity band via the specialization premium [Medium · Build provisionally] (R03 §C), and cheaper to own mindshare in — specialization is a channel multiplier, the narrower the niche the lower the cost to be its visible expert [Medium] (R04 §C). - Gated on: T2 — size of the bridge-core in each segment. R01 sized the full both-segment SAM ($200–450M/yr) but not the cross-border/both-sides slice (R01 #4, carried to R02). [Critical × Low · VALIDATION TRIGGER] — is the core large enough for a boutique?

D3 — Segmentation: one shared spine, two separate motions

Converge (one firm; shared, scarce assets): - The wedge/position: cross-border (FFIEC+OSFI) + both-sides + examiner-defensibility intersection [Medium] (R02 §F) — owned by Round 4. - The trust asset: regulated/examiner-survived proof, anchored on the bank side, lent down to SaaS (P10). - Cross-regime IP and the bridge insight (the thing no boutique competitor holds — R02 §C). - The senior dual-regime talent pool — the scarce shared resource that bounds everything (R05).

Diverge (separate motions — do not blend): | Dimension | SaaS motion | Bank motion | |---|---|---| | Buyer | Founder / CFO (brief S17) | CISO / CRO / risk officer (charter P2) | | JTBD | Unblock the deal/round | Survive the exam & the board | | Cycle | Weeks–months; faster | Months+; slower, heavier (R04 §E) | | Channel | Investor/accelerator + founder peer nets + GRC-platform/auditor ecosystem (R04 §E) | FS-ISAC/CB-ISAC peer-CISO + ABA/ICBA/CCUA/CBA associations; never examiner-led (R04 §E) | | Value metric | Revenue/deal unblocked (R03 §B) | Examiner defensibility + avoided enforcement (R03 §B/§D) | | Pricing shape | Fixed-fee outcome → stage-scaled retainer ($8–12K→$12–22K/mo, R01 §D) | Project + exam-cycle retainer ($25–75K+ TPRM/migration, R01 §D) |

  • Beachhead & sequencing deferred to Round 2 (per MODERATOR.md arc). Round 1 records the asymmetry Round 2 must weigh: trust and durability favor a regulated anchor (P10, P6/R02 §E, R03 §D measured WTP); volume, speed, and near-term cash favor SaaS (R01 §B, R04 §E faster channel). The capacity constraint (R05) means you cannot lead with both — that is the heart of P12's "pick one."
  • Gated on: T4 — dual-regime senior talent availability [Critical × Low · VALIDATION TRIGGER] (R05 trigger #2). How many quadrants can actually be staffed bounds how aggressively the segmentation can be run.

D4 — Trigger map (what fires a buy)

SaaS triggers - First six-figure enterprise/bank deal in pipeline → procurement security questionnaire (~Series A, $1–2M ARR). [Fact · multi-source · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S17][S18]). - Investor/round condition — SOC 2 as VC operational-maturity milestone. [Opinion/Fact · Secondary/blog · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (R04 §E; ~70% of VCs prefer SOC 2-compliant — blog-tier). - Selling into a bank specifically → heavier dual-regime diligence; start ~6 months ahead. [Opinion · Vendor · Medium · Supporting] (brief [S19]) — the bridge trigger on the SaaS side. - AI feature pulling AI/ML into SOC 2 scope / ISO 42001 demand. [Fact/Forecast · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (brief [S38][S46]) — emerging, dated by EU AI Act timing.

Bank triggers - Exam cycle / MRA / exam finding → remediation buy. [Opinion · Primary · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R04 §E — exam findings drive demand, not origination). - FFIEC CAT sunset (31 Aug 2025) → re-baseline to NIST CSF 2.0. [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build] (brief [S26]). - Third-party / vendor-risk program build-out under joint US guidance / OSFI B-10 + E-21. [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build] (brief [S28][S34]). - OSFI Streamlined Framework (25 Jun 2026) → provincial CUs continuing federally + fintechs becoming FRFIs. [Fact · Primary · High · Supporting · Build] (brief [S15]) — the cross-over trigger that physically moves a buyer from vendor side to bank side. - New-vendor onboarding / M&A cyber due diligence. [Fact · Vendor · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (brief [S34]; R01 §D).

The bridge trigger (touches both ICPs at once — the wedge's natural entry point) - A SaaS vendor selling to a regulated FI inherits B-13/B-10/FFIEC obligations; the bank, accountable for that vendor, must evidence the oversight. [Opinion(regulator-paraphrase)/Fact · Primary · Medium–High · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S36][S28][S34]). This single event is where WNW's both-sides cross-border fluency is uniquely valuable — and the most efficient proof-of-demand to instrument first.

Remaining dissent (carried, not resolved)

  • P1: narrowing the SaaS ICP to the bridge-core risks starving pipeline before the slow bank motion matures; the perimeter must be genuinely resourced, not nominal. → Round 2 (sequencing) + Round 5 (packaging).
  • P12: the entire intersection ICP rests on unproven demand (T1) and unproven dual-regime staffing (T4); it is a working target, not a market. The "pick one beachhead and dominate" alternative remains live and is the central question of Round 2. → Round 2.
  • P2/P10 vs P1: identity-anchor (regulated) vs funding-anchor (SaaS) — agreed these are different axes; the firm's identity anchors regulated, its near-term cash may anchor SaaS. The reconciliation of the two is a sequencing call. → Round 2.

Validation triggers consolidated (for the synthesis register)

  • T1 — Intersection demand. Do buyers want one firm spanning FFIEC+OSFI and both sides, vs a single-regime specialist or a platform? [Critical × Low] NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL: buyer interviews, 8–12 per segment. (R02 #2; R03 #1).
  • T2 — Bridge-core size. How many SaaS firms sell into regulated FIs cross-border; how many small/mid FIs have cross-border / Streamlined-path exposure? [Critical × Low] (R01 #4 → R02).
  • T3 — SaaS-side WTP. No independent budget series exists for SaaS (unlike the bank CSBS series). [Critical × Low] NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL: buyer pricing probe. (R03 #1).
  • T4 — Dual-regime senior talent. Can the staffing for the core be hired/built? [Critical × Low] NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL: dual-regime talent census. (R05 #2).

Moderator's quality note (intervention check)

No defect logged. Personas stayed distinct (P1 breadth/volume, P2 depth/defensibility, P6 structural map, P10 trust mechanics, P12 gate); genuine disagreement was forced before each decision and the Skeptic took the last challenge each time; every market claim is grounded in a research file or the brief, or carried as an explicit risk-weighted validation trigger. One honest caution recorded inside the transcript: the "regulatory bridge" is the spine of this round, and while its mechanism is Primary/High (regulator guidance), the demand for a single firm to span it is Critical×Low (T1) — the round is careful to treat the intersection ICP as a gated working target, not a proven finding, exactly as the R02/R03 gate sign-offs require. No moderator-interventions.md entry created (no defect across R00–R01).

round: 2 title: Demand and timing thesis date: 2026-06-27 moderator: Moderator (neutral chair) personas_convened: P7 Regulatory & Frameworks Authority · P6 Competitive & Market Analyst · P5 GTM & Demand Engine Lead · P2 Regulated Buyer · P12 Strategic Skeptic inputs: research/01-market-sizing.md (sizing/flow) · research/02-competitive-whitespace.md (encroachment timing, wedge durability) · research/04-channel-acquisition.md (per-segment channel compounding profiles) · research/00-source-brief.md (Part B demand drivers + regulatory timeline) · rounds/round-01-icp.md (the deferred beachhead decision, identity-vs-funding anchor) note: R06 (regulatory-primaries) and R10 (ai-governance-demand) are PENDING, not accepted. Where this round touches AI-advisory demand or regulatory primary texts, it uses the brief's own claims AT THE BRIEF'S OWN CONFIDENCE (which explicitly labels AI-advisory a Forecast) and does not over-reach beyond accepted research. Round 2 — Demand and timing thesis

The question on the table

Round 1 defined two bridged ICPs and an identity anchored on the regulated side, then explicitly deferred the beachhead and sequencing decision to this round, under the R05 capacity bound (you cannot lead with both). Round 2 owes two decisions:

  1. The demand thesis ("why now"). The brief lists a stack of demand drivers (FFIEC CAT sunset, OSFI B-13/B-10/E-21, the Streamlined Framework, breach economics, cyber insurance, AI governance). The decision is not "is there demand" — it is which of these drivers actually convert to billable advisory, as opposed to tooling/platform demand, and at what confidence. A driver that pushes a buyer to buy Vanta is not a driver that pushes them to retain WNW.
  2. The sequencing. Which motion leads (SaaS vs bank), and US-vs-Canada timing. This is where P12's "pick ONE and dominate" gets resolved. Round 1 recorded the asymmetry to weigh: trust + durability + the only independently-measured WTP favor a regulated anchor; volume + speed + near-term cash favor SaaS. Round 1 also separated two axes that get conflated — identity-anchor (regulated) vs funding-anchor (SaaS) — and instructed Round 2 to reconcile them via sequence, not by choosing one and discarding the other.

A standing caution carried into this round (brief's own flag): AI-advisory demand is a FORECAST — "whether this translates into billable advisory volume rather than tooling demand is not yet measured" (brief [S39][S46], line 179/289). This round must not let the most exciting driver become a load-bearing one.

The reframing the room converged on first: sort every driver by advisory-conversion, not by size

Before persona positions, one analytic move reframed the demand question and is recorded up front because all five personas accepted it as the right axis (P7 proposed it; P12 stress-tested it; it held). The brief's drivers are real at Primary/High as regulatory facts. But a regulatory fact creates demand for something, and the strategy only cares about the slice that becomes billable senior-judgment advisory — because R05 established WNW is supply-bound on exactly those senior hours, and R02 established the durable wedge is the layer platforms cannot automate. So the right question for every driver is: does this convert to judgment work, or to a platform subscription?

Demand driver Regulatory fact (confidence) Converts to billable ADVISORY? Timing shape
OSFI B-13 / B-10 / E-21 operationalization (Canada) [Fact · Primary · High] (brief [S33][S34][S35]) High — principles-based by design; you cannot automate a principle the way you automate a checklist; small/mid FRFIs are still "operationalizing" (brief line 98). Judgment-heavy. Durable / ongoing. The engine, not a wave.
Third-party / vendor-risk cascade (joint FDIC/Fed/OCC guidance + B-10; third-party breach share doubled 15→30%) [Fact · Primary · High] (brief [S28][S22]) High — TPRM is bespoke, relationship-by-relationship judgment; this is the bridge's content (R01 §regulatory-bridge). Durable + rising (third-party share doubling is a fresh accelerant).
FFIEC CAT sunset → NIST CSF 2.0 re-baseline (US, 31 Aug 2025) [Fact · Primary · High] (brief [S26]) High but — re-baselining + the new Govern function (board-level accountability) is judgment/narrative work, not a tool install. DECAYING wave. The event is ~10 months old; the migration window is finite. "Ride it now," not a durable engine.
OSFI Streamlined Framework (Canada, launched 25 Jun 2026 — two days ago) [Fact · Primary · High] (brief [S15]) High per entrant — green-field FRFIs/continuing CUs have no B-13/B-10/E-21 program yet = whole-program advisory; it is the literal vendor→bank bridge event. Brand-new; volume/velocity UNKNOWN (phased, risk-based approvals = slow ramp). Forecast on size.
SaaS SOC 2 / deal-unblock trigger [Fact · multi-source · Medium] (brief [S17][S18]) Low-to-Medium and FALLING — this is the most automatable layer; Vanta/Drata + Cynomi-class platforms are compressing it (R02 §D/E). Converts increasingly to tooling, not advisory. High volume, commoditizing fast.
Cyber insurance (underwriting pushes MFA/EDR; 41% first-submission denial) [Fact · Major/single-origin · Medium] (brief [S43], Marsh/Coalition) Low — drives control implementation (tooling/MSSP), thin advisory slice; figures single-origin (brief [S42][S43][S293]). Backdrop pressure, not a primary advisory channel.
AI governance (ISO 42001, NIST AI RMF, EU AI Act high-risk Aug 2026) [Forecast · Mixed · Low-Medium] (brief [S38][S46][S39]) UNPROVEN — brief's explicit flag: tooling-vs-advisory split "not yet measured" (line 179); EU dates may slip to Dec 2027 (Omnibus, brief [S39]). Emerging option, dates moving. Not a pillar.

The pattern is the load-bearing finding: the drivers that convert to durable billable advisory are precisely the principles-based, examiner-facing, judgment-heavy ones — and they cluster on the regulated/bank side. The highest-volume drivers (SOC 2, insurance) convert mostly to tooling and are the most compressed. This is the same wedge R02 found (un-automatable layer), the same premium R03 priced (specialization), and the same place R05 says scarce senior hours earn the most. The demand thesis and the wedge are the same shape.

Persona positions (strongest case each; argument grounded in evidence)

P7 — The Regulatory & Frameworks Authority: "The durable demand is principles-based supervision, and right now the freshest of it is Canadian."

Table-stakes vs edge is my job. Three regulatory facts carry real, advisory-converting demand, and they read differently in Ottawa than in Washington.

  • The durable engine is OSFI's principles-based stack. B-13 (effective 1 Jan 2024), B-10 (third-party), and E-21 (operational resilience) are principles, not a control checklist — 17 principles across three domains, aligned to NIST CSF and CIS (brief [S33][S34]). [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build]. You cannot ship a platform that "does" a principle; an FI has to interpret it and defend the interpretation. That is billable judgment, recurring, and small/mid FRFIs are still operationalizing it (brief line 98). This is the most reliable demand in the whole stack.
  • The US has a genuine event, but it is decaying. The FFIEC CAT sunset (31 Aug 2025) forces a re-baseline to NIST CSF 2.0, whose new Govern function elevates board-level accountability (brief [S26][S32]). [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build]. Re-baselining is advisory work — but it is a one-time migration, now ~10 months in flight. A boutique cannot scale into a finite wave through a slow channel. Treat CAT as "demand we can ride for proof," not "demand we can build a firm on."
  • The single freshest event is the Streamlined Framework — and it is the bridge made literal. OSFI's framework, launched 25 June 2026 — two days ago, lets provincial credit unions continue federally and fintechs ("innovators") become federally-regulated deposit-takers, with phased risk-based approval (brief [S15]). [Fact · Primary · High · Supporting · Build]. Every entity that crosses that bridge is a green-field regulated institution with no B-13/B-10/E-21 program — whole-program advisory demand, and it physically moves a buyer from the vendor side to the bank side. This is the cross-over trigger Round 1 named.

My nuance the others gloss: the freshest, least-crowded regulatory tailwind right now is Canadian (Streamlined just launched; the US wave is aging). That is a reason not to treat Canada as a distant afterthought.

Concession: principles-based demand is the slowest to convert to a signed engagement and the heaviest to deliver (R05 — deep regulated clients consume the most senior hours). High-conversion does not mean fast cash. And the Streamlined cohort's size and velocity are unknown — phased approvals could trickle for years.

P6 — The Competitive & Market Analyst: "Whichever driver you ride, you ride it into the path of the platforms — so ride the one above the automation line."

Map the demand against the competitors moving on it now. The SaaS-side volume drivers (SOC 2, insurance controls) are exactly where encroachment is fiercest and accelerating: Vanta/Drata service-partner programs and Cynomi's $37M Series B AI vCISO platform (Apr 2025, ~2× throughput/human) are eating evidence collection, control mapping, baseline reporting (R02 §D/E). [Fact · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally]. So a demand thesis built on SOC 2 volume is a thesis built on a melting iceberg — you would be selling the exact layer that is being automated to a near-zero price (~$4,999 bundled CPA; ~60% claimed consult-fee cut, R02 §E, illustrative).

The advisory-converting drivers P7 named (B-13/B-10 principles, TPRM, examiner-facing re-baselining) sit above that automation line — which is also why R02 found the intersection vacancy there. The demand thesis and the white-space are the same place. That is the coherent read.

My warning on sequencing, against my own competitive map: "both-sides alone is occupied" (Echelon, IS Partners, Compass IT — all US, R02 §B). If you lead by chasing SaaS SOC 2 volume to fund the firm, you enter the most crowded and most compressed segment, against incumbents and platforms, with no differentiation — the me-too zone. The cross-border (FFIEC+OSFI) axis is the thin one (R02 §C); the differentiation only exists if Canada/OSFI fluency is in the offer from the start.

Concession: the cross-border vacancy's demand is still unverified (R02 #2, the gate residual) — existence is not appetite. I can tell you where the competitors aren't; I cannot yet tell you a buyer wants the gap filled.

P5 — The GTM & Demand Engine Lead: "Demand that converts to advisory is worthless if I can't build a repeatable path to it — and the only fast path is the SaaS-side channel."

I optimize for where the next ten clients actually come from, repeatably. R04 settled the channel asymmetry and it dominates the sequencing decision more than the demand mix does:

  • The SaaS channel is fast, digital, platform-mediated — it compounds quickly (investor/accelerator nodes, founder peer networks, the GRC-platform partner/auditor ecosystem). [Fact · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R04 §E).
  • The bank channel is slow, association- and peer-gated, trust-heavy — it compounds slowly and defends well (FS-ISAC/CB-ISAC peer-CISO, ABA/ICBA/CCUA/CBA), and crucially examiners do not refer vendors (R04 §E, corrected). [Fact · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally].

Here is the chicken-and-egg that decides sequencing: the bank channel's entry ticket is examiner-survived references ("have you done this in a regulated shop?" — P2's charter, R03 §D). A brand-new boutique does not have them yet. You cannot lead with the regulated buyer when you lack the very proof that buyer demands. So "lead bank-first" is not a channel that exists for WNW on day one — it is a channel you have to earn your way into.

My push: lead through the channel that is open and fast — the SaaS side — and specifically through the bridge-subset (SaaS vendors selling into regulated FIs), because that buyer (a) is reachable on the fast SaaS channel, (b) pays the deal-unblock value metric where the contract dwarfs the fee (R03 §B = real near-term cash and WTP), and (c) the delivery is regulated content (B-13/B-10/FFIEC dual-regime readiness) that manufactures the examiner-facing references the bank channel requires. The bridge is the only beachhead where the fast channel produces the slow channel's entry ticket.

My own worry (the opposing case R04 told me to keep live): the bridge-subset may be too narrow to fill a funnel — a boutique cannot out-publish its way to visibility in a sliver, and if the bridge-subset is small (Round 1 T2, unsized), I am building a demand engine on a hypothesis. Expertise-led origination has to be instrumented from day one, not assumed (R04 #2).

P2 — The Regulated Buyer: "If your references are all SaaS startups, I won't put you in front of my examiner. Earn my side, don't bolt it on."

The demand thesis is right that my side is where the durable, defensible money is — I have the only independently-measured budget line in this whole study (smallest community banks spend 50–64% of consulting on compliance, ten-year CSBS series, R03 §D). [Fact · Major · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally]. I am slow and heavy, but I renew and I pay for judgment, not hours.

But I have a hard objection to "lead through the SaaS channel." Round 1 already recorded my line: "we serve both software companies and banks" can read as a liability — a startup shop dabbling in banking. If WNW spends two years building a book of SaaS SOC 2 logos and then knocks on my door, the identity is wrong and the trust does not transfer (P10's one-directional rule, Round 1).

Where P5 wins me over — conditionally: the bridge-subset's delivery is not generic startup SOC 2. It is "we took a software vendor through a regulated bank's B-13/B-10/FFIEC third-party diligence." That is a reference in my language, about my supervisory world, demonstrating the dual-regime judgment I actually pay for. If the bridge work is positioned and delivered as regulated-vendor-diligence advisory (not as cheap SOC 2), then the references it builds are the ones that earn my trust later. That is the difference between earning my side and bolting it on.

My condition, therefore: the master narrative anchors on my side from day one (Round 1 D1 stands), even while the cash comes through the bridge. The firm must read as a regulated-risk firm that also serves the vendors in my supply chain — never as a startup firm reaching for banks.

P12 — The Strategic Skeptic: the last challenge (steelman the opposites)

Three hard pushes before anything is recorded.

  1. Steelman pure bank-first. P7 says the durable, high-conversion, measured-WTP demand is bank-side and the timing windows (CAT decaying now, Streamlined fresh now) are bank-side. If those windows are real and time-sensitive, why route around them through a SaaS sliver? The honest answer the room must give is the chicken-and-egg (P5/R04): bank-first has no channel and no references on day one, and it is the most capacity-heavy book (R05). I accept the route-around — but only because the channel and reference facts are Medium-grounded, not because bank demand is weaker. Record that bank-first loses on access, not on demand quality — those are different, and if the reference problem could be solved another way (a senior hire who brings examiner references), bank-first comes right back on the table. That's a real fork, not a closed one.

  2. Steelman pure SaaS-volume-first (ignore the bridge). Bigger pool (~10–11K eligible, R01 §B), fastest channel, fastest cash. Why not just take the volume and worry about identity later? Because R02 says that lands you in the most crowded, most compressed, most platform-threatened, most me-too zone, building the wrong trust asset (P10). The bridge is the discipline that keeps the SaaS channel without the SaaS commodity trap. Fine — but that discipline only pays if the bridge-subset is big enough to be a beachhead, and T2 (bridge-core size) is unsized and Critical×Low. You are choosing a beachhead you have not measured.

  3. The "pick one and dominate" reckoning. I have been carrying this since R02. Here is the resolution I will accept and the one I will not. I will not accept "we span both sides and both regimes from day one" — that is the four-quadrant fantasy R05's capacity finding kills and R02's demand-gate flags. I will accept "dominate the bridge" if and only if the bridge is genuinely ONE thing to dominate: one buyer (the SaaS founder/CFO selling into FIs), one channel (SaaS-side fast), one value metric (deal-unblock), one content spine (dual-regime vendor diligence). That is a focused beachhead, not a straddle. The thing you defer is the bank-direct motion and Canada market entry — you do not run them in parallel; you earn into them. If the plan keeps that discipline, "pick one" is satisfied. If it quietly becomes "do everything but call it a bridge," it is not.

My last condition before any decision is recorded: every load-bearing claim here that rests on bridge-subset demand (T1), bridge-core size (T2), SaaS-side WTP (T3), dual-regime staffing (T4) is still Critical×Low. Round 2 may set a direction; it may not declare a proven market. And add the new one this round exposes: does any of this regulatory demand actually convert to billable advisory rather than tooling — that is the demand thesis's own gate.

Forced disagreement → reconciliation (Skeptic gets the last word before each decision)

The room split cleanly and did not converge cheaply: - P7 pulled toward bank-side demand quality and a Canadian-first timing read. - P5 pulled toward the SaaS channel as the only fast, repeatable path and toward the bridge as the entry. - P2 resisted any SaaS-led identity but conceded if the bridge delivers regulated-content references. - P6 warned that the SaaS-volume route is the compression/me-too trap and that the differentiation requires Canada/OSFI in the offer from day one. - P12 refused both pure plays and demanded the bridge prove it is one focused thing, all gated.

The reconciliation that survived every challenge separates three distinct questions the room kept fusing: - Demand quality (where the durable advisory money is): regulated side. (P7, P6, P2 agree; grounded R02/R03/R05.) - Demand access (where a day-one boutique can actually originate, fast, with cash): SaaS-side channel, specifically the bridge-subset. (P5/R04 channel asymmetry; P2's chicken-and-egg.) - Identity (what the firm reads as): regulated, from day one — earned through the bridge's regulated-content delivery, not asserted cold and not surrendered to SaaS logos. (P2/P10, reconciling Round 1 D1 as a sequence.)

Bank-first optimizes quality but fails access; SaaS-volume-first optimizes access but corrupts quality and identity. The bridge is the only sequence where the fast channel (access) delivers regulated content (quality) that earns the regulated identity (P10) and manufactures the references that open the slow bank-direct channel later. That is the reconciliation of the funding-anchor/identity-anchor split Round 1 handed forward: funding flows through the SaaS-side bridge; identity anchors regulated; the two are reconciled by sequence, exactly as instructed.

P12's last challenge before recording: "You have chosen a beachhead you have not sized (T2) and whose demand you have not observed (T1/T5)." Acknowledged and built in — the sequencing decision is recorded as a directional commitment gated on T1/T2/T3/T4 and the new T5, with the bridge trigger named as the fastest, cheapest demand proof to instrument first (Round 1 D4 already flagged it as the single event touching both ICPs).

DECISIONS

D5 — The demand thesis: durable advisory demand is the un-automatable judgment layer of the regulatory operationalization wave; volume demand is the most automatable layer

"Why now" is not "there is a lot of demand." It is: the regulatory stack is converting from rules-on-paper to operationalized supervision right now, and the principles-based, examiner-facing, third-party-diligence parts of that conversion are billable senior judgment that platforms cannot automate — which is the same wedge (R02), premium (R03), and best-use-of-scarce-hours (R05) the deliberation has independently reached three times.

  • Primary advisory engine (build on it): OSFI B-13/B-10/E-21 operationalization + the third-party/vendor-risk cascade (joint US guidance + B-10; third-party breach share doubled 15→30%). [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build] (brief [S33][S34][S28][S22]). Durable, principles-based, judgment-heavy, examiner-facing.
  • Ride-it-now proof event (use, don't build the firm on): FFIEC CAT sunset → NIST CSF 2.0 re-baseline + new Govern function. [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build, but timing-bounded] (brief [S26][S32]). High advisory-conversion but a decaying finite wave (~10 months in flight) — a source of near-term US engagements and proof, not a durable engine.
  • Bridge accelerant (real, unsized): OSFI Streamlined Framework (launched 25 Jun 2026) — green-field FRFIs/continuing CUs needing whole programs; the literal vendor→bank crossover. [Fact · Primary · High · Supporting · Build on mechanism; Forecast on volume] (brief [S15]).
  • Volume backdrop, mostly tooling (do NOT anchor advisory demand on it): SaaS SOC 2 deal-unblock trigger (compressing toward platform price, R02 §D/E) and cyber insurance (drives control implementation, thin advisory slice, single-origin figures). [Fact · Medium/single-origin · Critical/Supporting · Use with caveat] (brief [S17][S18][S43]).
  • Forecast option, not a pillar: AI governance (ISO 42001 / NIST AI RMF / EU AI Act). [Forecast · Low-Medium · Supporting · Do not build on] — the brief's own flag stands: billable-advisory-vs-tooling split is unmeasured and EU dates may slip to Dec 2027 (brief [S39][S46], line 179). Instrument it; do not stake the thesis on it. Feeds R10 (pending).
  • Rests on: the regulatory facts at Primary/High (brief); the advisory-vs-tooling wedge at Medium (R02 §E); specialization premium at Medium (R03 §C); supply-bound finding (R05).
  • Gated on: T5 — advisory-vs-tooling conversion. That these drivers create demand is Primary/High; that the demand converts to billable senior advisory rather than self-serve tooling is an inference. [Critical × Low · VALIDATION TRIGGER] — same buyer-probe family as T1/T3 (one buyer engagement closes them together).

D6 — Sequencing: lead with the bridge-subset via the SaaS-side fast channel (US-first), earning the regulated identity through delivery; compound into the bank-direct motion; carry Canada/OSFI as differentiation from day one and enter it as the second wave

This is the resolution of "pick one and dominate." The one thing to dominate is the bridge — not "both sides," not "both regimes at once."

Beachhead (Phase 1): the bridge-subset — Series A–C software companies selling into regulated FIs (especially cross-border) — entered through the SaaS-side fast channel (investor/accelerator + founder peer nets + GRC-platform/auditor ecosystem, R04 §E). One buyer, one channel, one value metric (deal-unblock, R03 §B), one content spine (dual-regime vendor diligence). This is what satisfies P12's "one focused thing." - Why this beachhead: it is the only one where the fast channel (access) produces regulated content (quality) that builds examiner-facing references (the bank channel's entry ticket) while delivering near-term cash and WTP (deal-unblock value metric). It captures the same regulatory tailwind as bank-first (the bridge trigger is B-13/B-10/FFIEC cascading) through the channel a day-one boutique can actually run.

Compound (Phase 2): the bank-direct motion — the regulated buyer, the durable/highest-WTP engine (CSBS-measured, R03 §D), the slow association-gated channel (R04 §E). Not run in parallel; earned into as the bridge accumulates examiner-facing references and dual-regime delivery proof. This is where the Round 1 identity anchor cashes out.

Identity (all phases): anchored regulated from day one (Round 1 D1 stands) — the firm reads as a regulated-risk firm that serves the vendors in the supervisory supply chain, earning the anchor through the bridge's content, never surrendering it to SaaS commodity logos (P2's condition).

US vs Canada: - Cross-border (FFIEC + OSFI) fluency is in the offer, positioning, and IP from day one — it is the differentiation that makes the firm non-me-too (R02 §B/§C: US both-sides is occupied; cross-border is the vacancy), and it is cheap to assert in content before it is a full delivery market (specialization-as-channel-multiplier, R04 §C). - Market entry leads US for volume and channel speed (larger pool, R01 §B; faster digital channel, R04 §E), riding the CAT-sunset proof window while it lasts. - Canada is the second wave, timed to the Streamlined Framework cohort maturing into green-field program demand (brief [S15]) — entered once dual-regime delivery is proven, ~12–18 months behind US entry (directional). - Recorded live dissent (P7): the freshest, least-crowded regulatory tailwind right now is Canadian (Streamlined launched two days ago; US CAT wave aging). Deferring Canada too long may forfeit a first-mover window. Held open, gated on T6.

  • Rests on: channel asymmetry [Medium] (R04 §E); the chicken-and-egg reference logic [argument, grounded in R03 §D + R04 §E]; trust one-directionality [P10/Round 1]; encroachment-avoidance [Medium] (R02 §D/E); sizing/flow [Medium] (R01).
  • Gated on: T1 (intersection/bridge demand), T2 (bridge-core size — choosing an unsized beachhead), T3 (SaaS-side WTP), T4 (dual-regime staffing — bounds how fast Phase 2 + Canada can be entered), and new T6 (Streamlined cohort velocity). All Critical×Low / Forecast. The sequence is a directional commitment, not a proven market; the bridge trigger is the first thing to instrument for demand proof.

Remaining dissent (carried, not resolved)

  • P7: Canada-vs-US timing is a genuine open tension, not a settled "US-first." The Streamlined Framework is the single freshest, least-crowded advisory window and it is Canadian; a 12–18-month Canada deferral may be too slow. → gated on T6; revisit at Round 7 (GTM) and Round 8 (Canadian association channels).
  • P5: the bridge-subset may be too narrow to fill a repeatable funnel; a boutique cannot out-publish to visibility in a sliver. The expertise-led engine and the bridge-trigger demand must be instrumented from day one, not assumed. → Round 7. (Mirrors R04's standing opposing case.)
  • P12: bank-first lost on access (no channel/references day one), not on demand quality — if a senior hire arrives with examiner references, bank-first returns to the table. The fork is narrowed, not closed. And the entire sequence rests on T1/T2/T5 demand that has never been observed. → revisit if/when T4 staffing (a reference-bearing senior hire) resolves; Round 5/Round 9.
  • P2 (conditional concession, carried as a constraint): the bridge only earns the bank side if its delivery is positioned as regulated vendor-diligence advisory, not as cheap SOC 2. If the perimeter/commodity SaaS work dominates the firm's visible identity, the trust does not transfer. → Round 4 (positioning) + Round 5 (packaging) must enforce this.

Validation triggers (Round 2 additions + carried)

  • T5 — Advisory-vs-tooling conversion (NEW). Do the regulatory drivers (CAT re-baseline, B-13/B-10 operationalization, TPRM cascade) convert to billable senior advisory, or do buyers self-serve with platforms? [Critical × Low] NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL: buyer interviews / win-loss — of FIs and bridge-subset vendors that faced these obligations, what fraction retained external advisory vs bought tooling, and at what ACV. Same buyer-probe family as T1/T3 (one engagement closes all three).
  • T6 — Streamlined Framework cohort velocity (NEW). How many provincial CUs / fintechs actually take the federal path under the Streamlined Framework, and how fast (phased approvals)? [Forecast · Low] — partly desk-answerable as OSFI publishes; feeds R06 (regulatory-primaries, pending). Bounds the Canada-second-wave timing in D6 and P7's dissent.
  • T1 — Intersection/bridge demand (carried, Round 1): do buyers want one firm spanning FFIEC+OSFI and both sides? [Critical × Low] (R02 #2; R03 #1).
  • T2 — Bridge-core size (carried, Round 1): how many SaaS firms sell cross-border into regulated FIs; the beachhead is chosen unsized. [Critical × Low] (R01 #4 → R02).
  • T3 — SaaS-side WTP (carried, Round 1): no independent budget series. [Critical × Low] (R03 #1).
  • T4 — Dual-regime senior talent (carried, Round 1): bounds Phase 2 + Canada entry speed; a reference-bearing senior hire would also reopen P12's bank-first fork. [Critical × Low] (R05 #2).

Moderator's quality note (intervention check)

No defect logged. Personas stayed distinct (P7 regulatory durability + Canada-timing nuance; P6 competitive-compression map; P5 channel-speed + bridge-access; P2 identity/trust guardrail; P12 gate + steelmanned both pure plays); genuine disagreement was forced (bank-quality vs SaaS-access vs identity were held apart and not fused) before each decision, and the Skeptic took the last challenge each time. Every market claim is grounded in an accepted research file or the brief at the brief's own confidence, or carried as an explicit risk-weighted validation trigger.

Two honest cautions recorded inside the transcript: (1) R06 (regulatory-primaries) and R10 (ai-governance-demand) are pending — this round deliberately held AI-advisory demand at the brief's own Forecast/Low grade and did not let it become load-bearing, and carried T6 (Streamlined velocity) to R06 rather than over-reaching on primary text not yet pulled. (2) The sequencing decision (D6) commits to a beachhead that is unsized (T2) and whose demand is unobserved (T1/T5) — it is recorded as a directional commitment, gated on the buyer probe, with the bridge trigger named as the fastest demand proof to instrument, exactly as the R02/R03 gate sign-offs require. No moderator-interventions.md entry created (no defect across R00–R02).

round: 3 title: Competitive landscape and white space date: 2026-06-27 moderator: Moderator (neutral chair) personas_convened: P6 Competitive & Market Analyst · P4 Positioning Strategist · P3 Boutique Operator · P7 Regulatory & Frameworks Authority · P12 Strategic Skeptic inputs: research/02-competitive-whitespace.md (the two-axis teardown; encroachment D/E; white-space verdict F) · research/01-market-sizing.md (niche-too-small structural moat; SOM capacity-bound) · research/03-pricing-value.md (specialization premium = where margin survives compression) · research/05-capacity-economics.md (supply-bound; platform leverage = commodity layer only; dual-regime talent = web-unmeasured sliver) · research/00-source-brief.md (provider archetypes Part B Task 2; Big-4 archetype [S5]; productized-vCISO floor [S30b]) · rounds/round-01-icp.md (the regulatory bridge spine; core/perimeter) · rounds/round-02-demand.md (D5 advisory-vs-tooling line; D6 the bridge beachhead; demand-quality = white-space = same place) note: R06 (regulatory-primaries) and R07 (trust-mechanics) are PENDING, not accepted.
