Round 5 — Service design and packaging

The question on the table

Round 4 ended with a position, a wedge, and a "not for," and then handed Round 5 a packaging assignment, not a fresh debate: the firm must be able to DO commodity SOC-2 perimeter work for cash WITHOUT POSITIONING on it; the lead package = the BRIDGE engagement (unblocks the FI deal + manufactures the examiner-facing reference); core = senior hours/priced above commodity; perimeter = platform-leveraged/NOT senior hours; and P1's dissent — perimeter must be genuinely resourced or SaaS pipeline starves (R04 → Round 5). So this round does not relitigate who the buyer is or what the position is. It builds the offer architecture that delivers that position inside the binding constraint R05 made non-negotiable: WNW is supply-bound, not demand-bound. Senior dual-regime judgment-hours are the scarce resource.

This is the round where the strategy meets the spreadsheet. Every package the room proposes must answer two questions at once, and a package that answers only one is cut:

  1. Does the buyer recognize and want it? (P1/P2 own this — and the bridge buyer of D11 is the lead.)
  2. Can it be staffed at the senior-hour ceiling without collapsing the margin knife-edge? (P3/P11 own this — and they hold a veto.)

The forced disagreement is structural and built into the roster: - P1 (SaaS Buyer) pulls every offer toward productized, fixed-fee, time-bounded, outcome-priced work and resists open-ended retainers as consulting theater. - P2 (Regulated Buyer) pulls toward depth, documented credentials, regulated-market proof, and a heavier engagement that survives an examiner's diligence file (SR 24-2). - P8 (Pricing & Packaging Architect) pushes value-metric packaging and an explicit expansion architecture — the land-and-expand ladder is where boutique LTV actually comes from. - P3 (Operator) grounds every offer in who delivers it at what utilization, and refuses anything that only the founders can staff. - P11 (Capacity Modeler) holds the hard floor: the catalog is gated on whether it survives the senior-hour ceiling. The per-advisor economics are a knife-edge on two variables — utilization and premium pricing — and dropping either collapses the firm to the generalist floor.

There is no Skeptic this round (the roster excludes P12 here). P11 carries the adversarial economic challenge, and the Moderator keeps P12's two live tensions — is the bridge core big enough to fill the firm's senior books? (the double-edged-smallness fork, gated on T2) and does the perimeter quietly starve the core of senior hours? — explicitly in the text and re-bound to the decisions.

Gate check on R06 / R08 (recorded so the next run does not mistake it for oversight)

Per the standing ledger rule, a pending research file is commissioned only if a Critical decision in this round would otherwise sit under-grounded. It would not, and neither R06 (regulatory-primaries) nor R08 (partnerships) is commissioned this round. Reasoning:

  • The packaging decisions rest on accepted files: R03 (value metrics, land-and-expand, specialization premium — accepted Medium), R05 (the supply-bound finding, the bandwidth ceiling, the per-advisor economics — accepted Medium), R07 (the two trust paths and the SR 24-2 documented-diligence mandate — accepted, with SR 24-2 at Primary/High), plus R01/R02/R04 decisions and the brief's service/price ladder.
  • The one place R06 could bite is whether the dual-regime crosswalk is a durable moat — but Round 3 (H3) already ruled the crosswalk is a delivery artifact, not a moat, held at Medium and flagged; packaging uses it as a speed/leverage artifact (D16), which does not require lifting H3 above Medium.
  • R08 (partnerships) feeds Round 8 (channel-as-partner), not the offer architecture. The perimeter's platform-leverage dependency (D16) does lean on the Cynomi/RealCISO-class leverage claim, which R05 already carries at Medium/COI with a pilot trigger (R05 trigger #5) — that is the correct cell; R08 would not change it.

Decision: proceed. No defect; no intervention entry.

The frame the room adopted first: package the two layers on two different delivery engines, not just two different prices

Before any single package was designed, P3 and P11 forced one structural decision that governs the whole catalog, and P1/P2/P8 accepted it. R01 D2 already named the core/perimeter split as a packaging instruction; R05 made it an economic necessity. The room's refinement: core and perimeter are not two price tiers of the same service — they are two services on two different delivery engines, and the dividing line is whether the work consumes a senior judgment-hour.

Working rule (adopted by all five): Every line item in the catalog declares its delivery engine before it declares its price. There are exactly two engines. The CORE engine = senior dual-regime judgment-hours (the scarce, supply-bound resource of R05; priced above the commodity band per R03 C; the visible identity per R04 D10). The PERIMETER engine = platform + junior/analyst leverage with senior QA only (the commodity/automatable layer R02 documented as compressing toward platform price; ~4–5× leverage on that layer only per R05 A; served for cash and pipeline; never the visible identity per R04 D10/D12). A package that quietly routes perimeter work onto the core engine fails both the margin test (P11) and the capacity test (P3) and is cut.

This rule is what lets the round honor two instructions that otherwise look contradictory: do perimeter work for cash (R04 D10; P1's "resource the perimeter") and never let it consume the senior hours the wedge needs (R05; P11's gate). The resolution is not "do less perimeter" — it is "deliver perimeter on a different engine." P1's dissent and P11's gate, which read as opposites, converge here: the perimeter must be genuinely resourced by a non-senior delivery layer, or it both starves the core and fails to relieve the SaaS pipeline. Resourcing it = staffing the non-senior engine, not stealing senior hours.

Persona positions (strongest case each; grounded in evidence)

P1 — The SaaS Buyer: "Sell me a result with a finish line, not a relationship with no end. Productize the bridge or I buy a platform and a generalist and hope."

I am the access end of the bridge and the firm's near-term cash (R04; R02 D6). Package for me wrong and the pipeline that funds the bank motion never fills.

  • What I buy is a bounded outcome. When a bank prospect's third-party security diligence packet stalls my deal (the bridge trigger, D11), I want "get me through this" with a scope, a price, and a date — the brief's own deal-trigger pattern (SOC 2/ISO gating a six-figure contract or an investor condition) is a finish line, not a journey [Fact · Vendor · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S17][S18]; R03 B). Sell me a "maturity program" and I hear theater and overhead (P1 charter).
  • The value metric I pay on is the deal unblocked, not your hours (R03 B SaaS metric = revenue/deal velocity unblocked). Fixed-fee, outcome-anchored. Value-based pricers win the larger engagements precisely because the buyer is buying the outcome — 51% of value-based consultants land $10K+ projects vs 39% of hourly billers [Fact · Secondary · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (Consulting Success 2023 survey, via R03 B). That is the structure I respond to.
  • My objection to the retainer is real but not absolute. I refuse an open-ended retainer with no deliverable. I do not refuse a retainer whose ongoing value I can name to my board — keeping my diligence posture current as I add the next three FI customers is a nameable, recurring outcome. Earn it off a delivered result; don't sell it cold on day one.

Concession: for the bridge subset (my D11/D9 concession, carried) the regulated depth IS the outcome, so I will pay the specialist premium (R03 C) for the firm that clears the bank's diligence fastest and most credibly — if the lead package has a finish line. And I concede a continuation retainer is not theater when it is tied to a defined ongoing value and entered after a delivered win, not before it. My hard line stays: the lead offer is productized with a date, or you lose the fast channel.

P2 — The Regulated Buyer: "Your 'package' becomes a line in my examiner's file. It has to be documented, methodical, and survivable — not a sprint with a slide deck."

I am the anchor end, the slower and heavier and more valuable motion, and I will not be packaged to P1's tempo.

  • My buying is a documented process, mandated, not a preference. The Interagency TPRM guidance requires me to assess and document a third party's qualifications, expertise, past performance, references, and independent reviews under board oversight [Fact · Primary · High · Critical · Build] (R07 §C; SR 24-2). So a bank-side package is not "delivered" when the work is done — it is delivered when it has produced examiner-legible artifacts: a documented methodology, a defensible file, named references, a board-presentable narrative. A bridge sprint that produces a persuasive deck but not a documented, examiner-survivable file does nothing for my diligence obligation.
  • My value metric is examiner defensibility and avoided enforcement (R03 B bank metric), and the stakes are quantifiable — Canadian AMPs run $10K–500K CAD, a clean exam and an avoided MRA are the measurable outcomes [Fact · Vendor/Primary · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S35]; R03 B). My WTP for this is structurally real and measured: the smallest community banks spend 50–64% of their consulting budget on compliance [Fact · Major · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (CSBS, via R03 D) — but the FDIC explicitly warns me off "costly and unnecessary" consultants [Opinion · Primary · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (FDIC, via R03 D), so I pay for judgment that survives an exam, not for commodity hours. Package me the judgment layer, documented; never the automatable layer.
  • The same-industry, regulated reference is my entry ticket (R07 §B-2: same-industry case studies carry ~37% higher credibility) — which is exactly why the bridge engagement's examiner-facing artifact matters to me even though it is sold to a SaaS company. That artifact, accumulated, is what lets me say yes before I am the firm's first bank.

Concession: I accept that I am earned into, not led with (R02 D6; R04). I accept the bank-side core can be entered through a bounded front door — a TPRM migration or an exam-prep project (R03 E land step) — provided that front door is delivered to my documentation standard and ladders into the deeper, examiner-cycle-aligned retainer. My hard line: the visible identity stays regulated-grade (R04 D10), and the bank package's artifacts are documented and defensible, or it is not a bank package — it is SaaS work wearing a bank costume, and my examiner sees through it.

P8 — The Pricing & Packaging Architect: "Productize the land, value-meter the expand, and design the cross-sell into the catalog. The boutique's money is in the ladder, not the logo."

The catalog's job is not to list services; it is to engineer the land-and-expand motion R03 proved is structurally dominant. Three moves.

  • Productize the lead (the land step) so it is repeatable and value-anchored. A productized service — fixed scope, fixed outcome, a clean value metric — is the only way a boutique sells a bounded result and keeps delivery repeatable (it satisfies P1's finish line and P3's repeatability simultaneously). The two segment-specific value metrics are already locked: SaaS = revenue/deal unblocked; bank = examiner defensibility + avoided AMP (R03 B). Price each land package on its segment's value metric, not on hours.
  • Engineer the expansion path into the architecture, because that is where the LTV is. Land-and-expand is not opportunism; it is structural: ~70% of professional-services revenue sits with existing clients, logo retention ~83–85%, mid-market NRR ~108%, and specialists retain +38% over generalists [Fact · Major/Secondary · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (SPI/First Page Sage/McKinsey, via R03 E). So the catalog must have explicit, designed rungs: land (bounded project) → expand (recurring retainer) → cross-sell (2nd framework / 2nd regime / 2nd side). The cross-border axis (FFIEC→OSFI) and the both-sides axis (SaaS↔bank) are not just positioning — they are the firm's richest cross-sell inventory.
  • The retainer is a hybrid, not a pure subscription, which is how P1's resistance dissolves. Pure outcome-pricing is hard to operationalize; the practical structure is base retainer + outcome anchor [Opinion · Vendor · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat] (Cycore, via R03 B). A continuation retainer with a named recurring value (posture maintenance, next-framework, next-regime) is not the open-ended retainer P1 refuses — it is a value-metered renewal, entered off a delivered land. The stage-scaled ladder the brief already shows ($8–12K → $12–22K/mo as company stage/risk rises) is itself a crude value metric [Fact · Vendor · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (brief [S30b]; R03 B).

Concession: the structure is what I own; the price points are Round 6's, and they sit on a COI-capped Medium band until a buyer probe returns (R03 #1). And I concede to P11: an expansion ladder that the firm cannot staff at each rung is a slide, not a strategy — the cross-sell inventory is only real if the second-regime/second-side delivery can be resourced without breaching the senior-hour ceiling. I design the ladder; P3/P11 decide how many rungs the firm can actually climb at once.

P3 — The Boutique Operator: "Tell me who delivers each line item and at what utilization, or it's not a service — it's a wish. And it cannot all be the founders."

I have run this firm. Every package on the table dies or lives on one question: who staffs it, and does it still work when the founders are busy selling?

  • The catalog must be deliverable on a layered team, not on heroes. The senior dual-regime advisor is the scarce resource (R05 C). If every package — including the commodity SOC-2 readiness — routes through a senior, the firm caps at 5–8 clients per founder and never scales (R05 A). The only way out is the layered pod: senior owns the judgment; a junior/analyst owns the evidence-collection, control-mapping, and first-pass reporting; a platform automates what it can (R02/R03's commodity layer; R05 A's ~4–5× leverage on that layer). The senior's hour is spent on interpretation and the examiner-facing call, not on filling spreadsheets.
  • Productization is a delivery instrument, not just a pricing one. A productized package with a templated methodology, a reusable dual-regime crosswalk artifact (R03 H3 — the crosswalk is a delivery artifact, not a moat), and a defined deliverable set is what makes the work repeatable by the pod and cuts senior-hours per client — which is the single most effective lever on the R05 ceiling besides hiring (R05 A moderator read: "productize to cut senior-hours per client"). P8's productization and my staffability are the same instrument seen from two sides.
  • Founder selling time is the hidden capacity tax. R05 D is decisive: loaded CAC is dominated by senior selling hours, not marketing spend — every hour a founder sells is an hour not delivered against the ceiling, so the CAC problem and the capacity problem are the same problem [Opinion/Moderator · Medium · Critical] (R05 D). The catalog must therefore favor packages that are easy to sell (productized, finish-lined, referenceable) and that originate through low-senior-hour channels (R04 expertise-led origination, referral) — packaging is a capacity decision, not just a marketing one.

Concession: I accept P2's bank-side core is genuinely senior-heavy and cannot be fully leveraged down — examiner-defensibility judgment is the wedge and does not 4–5× (R05 A). So I am not asking to leverage the core; I am asking to ring-fence it: leverage the perimeter hard, productize the core to shave its commodity sub-tasks down to the pod, and reserve the irreducible senior judgment-hours for the work only a senior can do. That is the only catalog I can staff.

P11 — The Unit-Economics & Capacity Modeler: the hard floor (the round's adversarial economic gate)

No Skeptic sits this round; I hold the floor. I do not ask whether buyers want the catalog — P1/P2 answer that. I ask whether the catalog survives the spreadsheet, and I have a veto.

  • The per-advisor model is a knife-edge on two variables, and the catalog is what tips it. R05 B is explicit: a senior advisor's ~$540–860K revenue and ~45–60% gross margin hold only on high utilization AND premium pricing simultaneously; drop either and margin collapses toward the SPI generalist floor (rev/consultant $199K, project margin 35.9%, EBITDA 9.8%) [Assumption/Fact · Low/Major · Critical · gate] (R05 B). Packaging controls both variables. Premium pricing depends on the catalog being wedge work (R03 C specialization premium), not commodity work priced at the floor. Utilization depends on the catalog being staffable on the right engine — every senior hour spent on a commodity task that a junior or a platform should have done is a direct hit to both margin and the capacity ceiling. So the catalog is not downstream of the economics; it is the lever that sets them.
  • The perimeter is a capacity test, not just a revenue line. This is where I bind P12's carried "perimeter-starves-the-core" tension. Perimeter work is justified only if it runs on the perimeter engine (platform + junior + senior QA). If it leaks onto the senior, it does the worst of both things: it consumes the scarce resource AND it dilutes the premium (the senior is now billing commodity work at — or below — commodity rates). The leverage that makes the perimeter safe is the Cynomi/RealCISO-class ~4–5× / ~70%-workload-cut — but that is a vendor self-claim on the automatable layer, COI-capped Medium, and the realized leverage on a regulated-adjacent book is likely lower [Opinion/Forecast · Vendor · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat / TRIGGER] (R05 A; R05 trigger #5). So the perimeter is approved with a pilot gate: prove the leverage on a real book before scaling the perimeter, or it silently becomes a senior-hour sink.
  • The expansion ladder is capacity-rationed. P8's cross-sell inventory (2nd framework / 2nd regime / 2nd side) is real LTV, but each rung consumes senior hours, and the deep engagements push toward the 3–6-client end of the ceiling, not the 5–8 end (R05 A/B). The firm cannot climb every rung for every client at once. The ladder is sequenced by what the current senior bench can deliver at target utilization — not by what the buyer would buy.
  • The double-edged-smallness fork is my open gate (P12, carried). The healthy LTV:CAC (~7–20×, R05 E) is healthy because delivery is capacity-rationed — it is not a signal that growth is easy. The unresolved question is whether the bridge core is big enough to fill the senior books the model needs (T2 — bridge-core size, Critical×Low). If the core is too thin, the firm either under-fills its seniors (utilization collapses, the knife-edge tips) or over-leans on the perimeter (premium collapses, the knife-edge tips the other way). I cannot close this; it is gated on T2 and R01's adoption/ACV trigger. I require it to stay live in the decision text, not be smoothed over by a tidy catalog.

Concession: the catalog can clear a healthy boutique margin — the model is favorable on demand, retention, NRR, and LTV:CAC (R05 E). I am not gating the existence of the business; I am gating the shape of the catalog. My conditions: (1) the core runs on senior hours and is priced above the commodity band; (2) the perimeter runs on the leverage engine and is pilot-gated before it scales; (3) the expansion ladder is sequenced to the deliverable senior-hour budget; (4) utilization and senior-hours-per-client are instrumented from day one (R05 → Round 9). Meet those and the catalog passes the floor.

Forced disagreement → reconciliation

The room split along two fault lines, and both resolve without averaging.

Fault line 1 — P1 (productized, finish-lined, no open retainer) vs P2 (heavy, documented, examiner-legible). This is the bridge again, expressed as packaging. It does not resolve into one package shaped like the average of P1 and P2. It resolves into two package families off one delivery spine (R04's "one spine, two proofs," now expressed as "one spine, two package families"): - The SaaS-side / bridge family is P1-shaped on the outside: productized, fixed-fee, outcome-anchored on deal unblocked, with a finish line. But its delivery is P2-grade on the inside — it produces a documented, examiner-legible artifact, because that artifact is both the bank's diligence requirement and the firm's reference-manufacturing engine (R02 D6; R07 §B-2/§C). The bridge package is the one place P1's finish-line and P2's documentation requirement point at the same deliverable. - The bank-side family is P2-shaped throughout: a bounded but documentation-heavy land (TPRM migration / exam prep), laddering into an examiner-cycle-aligned retainer, delivered on the senior-heavy core engine with examiner-legible artifacts. P1 does not get to make this one a sprint; P2 does not get to make the bridge package a 200-slide program.

Fault line 2 — P8 (engineer the expansion ladder; the LTV is in the rungs) vs P3/P11 (every rung must be staffable at the ceiling). Reconciled by making productization the shared instrument and the senior-hour budget the sequencer: - Productization serves P8 (a clean value metric per package) and P3 (a repeatable delivery recipe) and P11 (it shaves commodity sub-tasks off the senior, protecting both margin variables) — it is one instrument, three benefits. - The ladder is designed in full (P8) but climbed in sequence (P11): the catalog lists every rung, and the firm's capacity model decides how many rungs it offers at once, given the current senior bench and target utilization. The cross-sell inventory is real; it is just rationed, not free.

P11's last challenge before each decision (the floor's veto, standing in for the Skeptic's role): "Name the delivery engine and the senior-hour cost of every line item, or it does not enter the catalog. And keep the bridge-core-size fork (T2) live — a catalog this clean can hide the fact that we have not proven the core is big enough to fill the seniors it assumes." Acknowledged and built in — every package below declares its engine; the perimeter is pilot-gated; the ladder is capacity-sequenced; and the smallness fork is carried into the decision text and the trigger register.

DECISIONS

D13 — The offer architecture: a two-engine catalog (defended CORE on senior judgment-hours, leveraged PERIMETER on platform+junior), with explicit in/out boundaries

The catalog is organized first by delivery engine, not by service name, because the engine is what governs both the margin knife-edge (P11) and the capacity ceiling (P3). [Decision · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R01 D2; R04 D10; R05 A/B; R03 C).

CORE engine — senior dual-regime judgment-hours (the visible identity; priced above the commodity band; supply-bound; the wedge): - C1 — The Bridge Engagement (the lead/wedge package — specified in D14). SaaS-side, productized, dual-artifact. - C2 — Dual-regime advisory retainer (fractional vCISO with regulated depth). The SaaS-side expand rung: ongoing vendor-diligence posture, framework maintenance, next-FI-customer readiness. Stage-scaled (the brief's $8–12K → $12–22K/mo ladder as a crude value metric, brief [S30b]). Senior-led with pod support. - C3 — Examiner-Defensible TPRM / exam-prep engagement (bank-side land). Bounded project — TPRM program build or migration, or exam preparation — delivered to P2's documentation standard, producing examiner-legible artifacts (methodology, documented file, references) per SR 24-2 (R07 §C). Senior-heavy; pushes toward the 3–6 deep-client end of the ceiling (R05 A). - C4 — Bank risk-advisory retainer (examiner-cycle-aligned). The bank-side expand rung: ongoing program ownership tied to the exam cycle and board reporting. The heaviest, most valuable, slowest-to-earn engagement (P2; R03 D). - C5 — Cross-sell extensions (the ladder's top rungs): 2nd framework (e.g. ISO 27001 after SOC 2), 2nd regime (OSFI after FFIEC — the cross-border axis), 2nd side (a SaaS client's bank introduction; a bank's vendor population). Each is a senior-hour consumer, capacity-sequenced per D16.

PERIMETER engine — platform + junior/analyst with senior QA only (served for cash and pipeline; NEVER the visible identity; pilot-gated): - P-1 — Commodity SOC 2 / ISO readiness ("the readiness factory"). Evidence collection, control mapping, first-pass readiness and baseline reporting — the layer R02/R03 documented as compressing toward platform price. Delivered on the leverage engine, not by seniors. This is the perimeter P1 insists must be genuinely resourced and P11 insists must not touch a senior hour — both satisfied by routing it to the non-senior engine (the round's opening frame). It is a pipeline feeder into C1/C2 and a cash line, but per R04 D10 it is never positioned on.

What is IN (the visible identity): the dual-regime, judgment-layer, examiner-defensibility work — C1–C5. The firm markets the core and lets the perimeter be a quiet capability.

What is OUT (enforcing R04 D10's four exclusions, now as packaging boundaries): 1. Commodity SOC-2 as the positioned offer. The firm does P-1 for cash; it never makes it the visible face (R04 D10.1; R07 §D halo). [Decision · Medium · Critical] 2. Enterprise-bank / large-FI scope needing Big-4 scale — the deliberate upper boundary (R03 two-boundary frame; R04 D10.2). [Decision · Medium · Supporting] 3. Single-regime-only / single-side-only engagements with no cross-border or both-sides need — the crowded, compressing zone where WNW has no barrier (R03 H2; R04 D10.3). Served only opportunistically, never as a wedge. [Decision · Medium · Supporting] 4. Staff-aug / hourly bodies. The catalog sells judgment and outcomes, not hours — hourly billing forfeits the specialization premium that is the firm's only margin-survival above the commodity floor (R03 C; R05 B knife-edge; R04 D10.4). [Decision · Medium · Supporting]

D14 — The lead/wedge package: "The Bridge Engagement" — a productized, fixed-scope, dual-artifact package that unblocks the FI deal AND manufactures the examiner-facing reference

The single package the whole motion lands on first (R04 D11; R02 D6). It is designed to satisfy P1's finish-line and P2's documentation standard in the same deliverable, because for the bridge buyer they are the same purchase (R04 reconciliation). [Decision · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally]

  • Buyer & trigger: the Series A–C software company whose FI deal has stalled on a third-party security/vendor-diligence requirement citing FFIEC TPRM / OSFI B-10/B-13 (the bridge trigger, D11; brief [S28][S34][S36]).
  • Shape (P1): productized, fixed-scope, time-bounded, fixed-fee, anchored on the SaaS value metric — the regulated deal unblocked (R03 B). A finish line, not a journey. This is what keeps it sellable on low senior-selling-hours (R05 D) and recognizable to the fast channel.
  • Dual artifact (P2 + the reference engine): delivery produces two assets off one engagement — (a) a deal-unblock package the SaaS buyer hands its bank counterparty (the outcome P1 pays for), and (b) a documented, examiner-legible artifact (methodology + defensible file) that (i) satisfies the bank's SR 24-2 diligence requirement and (ii) becomes WNW's same-industry reference for the bank channel (R07 §B-2/§C; R02 D6). The bridge package is the firm's reference-manufacturing engine, not just a revenue line.
  • Delivery engine: CORE (senior dual-regime judgment), with the pod handling the commodity sub-tasks (evidence assembly, control mapping) and the senior owning the examiner-facing interpretation and the defensible file (D16). Productization shaves the senior-hour cost so the package fits the ceiling (P3/P11).
  • Why this and not a generic SOC 2: a platform/generic SOC 2 attests a control exists; the bridge package demonstrates the control survives a regulated vendor-diligence standard — the judgment layer the buyer cannot automate, cannot get cheaply from a giant, and cannot get from a single-regime shop (R04 D9/D12; R07 §E).
  • Value metric & pricing structure (points deferred to Round 6): fixed-fee on deal unblocked, structured to ladder into C2 (the dual-regime retainer) as the buyer adds further FI customers. Pricing points are Round 6's and sit on the COI-capped Medium band (R03 A); this round fixes only the structure.
  • Gated on: T1/T5 (is the bridge band wanted, and bought as advisory vs self-served tooling?), T7 (does the buyer recognize the frame?), T2 (is the bridge core big enough to fill senior books? — the smallness fork, P11/P12), and the R05 capacity ceiling (the package must not exceed deliverable senior hours).

D15 — The land-and-expand ladder, the two value metrics applied to packaging, and the retainer reconciliation

The catalog is engineered as a designed ladder (P8), climbed in capacity-sequenced rungs (P11), with the value metric segment-specific (R03 B). [Decision · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R03 B/E; R05 B/E).

The ladder (two segment tracks off one spine): - SaaS / bridge track: LAND = C1 Bridge Engagement (fixed-fee, value metric = deal unblocked) → EXPAND = C2 dual-regime retainer (stage-scaled, value = ongoing diligence-readiness as FI customers accumulate) → CROSS-SELL = C5 (2nd framework; 2nd regime via the cross-border axis; introduction to the buyer's bank counterparty = the 2nd side). - Bank track: LAND = C3 TPRM/exam-prep project (value metric = examiner defensibility + avoided AMP; brief [S35]) → EXPAND = C4 examiner-cycle retainer → CROSS-SELL = C5 (2nd regime; the bank's vendor population as new bridge-buyer pipeline = the 2nd side flowing the other direction).

The retainer reconciliation (P1 vs P8, resolved): the expand rung is a hybrid — base retainer + outcome anchor (R03 B; Cycore), entered off a delivered land, not sold cold, and named on a recurring value the buyer can defend (posture maintenance / next framework / next regime). This is not the open-ended retainer P1 refuses; it is a value-metered renewal (P1's concession). The stage-scaled band ($8–12K → $12–22K/mo) is itself a crude value metric scaling fee with stage/risk, not hours (brief [S30b]; R03 B).

The cross-sell inventory is the firm's richest LTV asset and its capacity test: the cross-border (FFIEC↔OSFI) and both-sides (SaaS↔bank) axes are unique cross-sell rungs no single-regime competitor holds (R02; R04 D9) — and each rung consumes senior hours, so the firm offers the rungs its bench can deliver at target utilization (D16; P11). Specialists retain +38% and expand better than generalists (R03 E), so the ladder compounds the wedge into LTV — conditional on staffing it (P11's gate).

  • Gated on: T2/R01 adoption-ACV (is the core big enough to support the ladder's assumed senior books? — the smallness fork), R03 #1 (buyer WTP / the premium over single-regime alternatives — pricing points), R03 #2 / R05 #1 (WNW's real renewal/NRR/expansion data — the LTV the ladder assumes).

D16 — The delivery model that staffs the catalog, and the capacity gate that prunes it

The catalog is only real if it can be staffed at the senior-hour ceiling without tipping the margin knife-edge. The delivery model is the round's hardest decision (P3/P11) and it gates D13–D15. [Decision · Medium · Critical · Build provisionally] (R05 A/B/C/D; R03 C; R02/R03 commodity-layer).

The layered pod (the unit of delivery): - Senior dual-regime advisor — owns the judgment: the examiner-facing interpretation, the defensible file, the board narrative, the dual-regime call. This is the scarce, supply-bound resource (R05 C); it does not 4–5× (R05 A). Ceiling: 5–8 light retainers OR 3–6 deep/regulated engagements per senior (R05 A). - Junior / analyst layer — owns the commodity sub-tasks even within a core engagement: evidence collection, control mapping, first-pass readiness, documentation assembly. This is the leverage that shaves senior-hours-per-client (R05 A moderator read; P3). - Platform (Cynomi/RealCISO-class) — automates the automatable layer (~4–5× / ~70% workload cut on that layer only), powering the perimeter engine (P-1) and the commodity sub-tasks of the pod. [Opinion/Forecast · Vendor · Medium · Supporting · Use with caveat / pilot-gated] (R05 A; R05 trigger #5).

The two engines, mapped to the catalog: - CORE engine (senior + pod): C1–C5. Senior owns judgment; pod + platform own the commodity sub-tasks; the senior hour is reserved for what only a senior can do. Productization (templated methodology, the dual-regime crosswalk as a delivery artifact per R03 H3) cuts the senior-hour cost per engagement (P3/P8 shared instrument). - PERIMETER engine (platform + junior + senior QA only): P-1. No senior delivery hours beyond QA — this is the structural answer to P1's "resource the perimeter" and P11's "perimeter must not starve the core": resource it on the non-senior engine.

The capacity gate (P11's veto, applied): 1. Every line item declares its engine and its senior-hour cost before it enters the catalog. (Done in D13.) 2. The perimeter is pilot-gated: the ~4–5× leverage is a COI-capped vendor claim; prove realized leverage on a real regulated-adjacent book before scaling P-1, or it silently becomes a senior-hour sink (R05 trigger #5; P11). 3. The expansion ladder is capacity-sequenced: the firm offers the rungs its current senior bench can deliver at target utilization, not the full inventory at once (P11; D15). 4. Founder-selling time is treated as capacity, not just CAC: packaging favors productized, finish-lined, referenceable offers that originate through low-senior-hour channels (R05 D; R04 expertise-led origination + referral) — packaging is a capacity decision (P3). 5. Hiring/apprenticeship is the only lever that lifts the ceiling: since the senior layer does not leverage (R05 A) and the dual-regime hire is the scarce bottleneck (R05 C / T4), the bench-and-apprenticeship plan is a first-order constraint on how fast the catalog can scale — handed to Round 9 (R05 → Round 9).

  • Gated on: T4 (can the dual-regime senior layer be staffed? — the moat-is-bottleneck gate, R05 C), R05 #1 (real utilization & senior-hours-per-engagement — recalibrates the 5–8/3–6 ceiling for regulated engagements, which may run heavier), R05 #5 (realized platform leverage on a regulated book — the perimeter pilot gate).

Remaining dissent (carried, not resolved)

  • P11/P12 — the double-edged smallness / bridge-core-size fork is OPEN. The catalog assumes the bridge core can fill the senior books the per-advisor model needs; T2 (bridge-core size) and R01's adoption/ACV trigger have not confirmed it. If the core is too thin, the firm either under-fills seniors (utilization tips the knife-edge) or over-leans on the perimeter (premium tips it the other way). Not closed here; gated on T2. → Round 6 (does the pricing hold at the achievable volume?) and Round 9 (instrument utilization and pipeline-to-core from day one).
  • P1/P11 — the perimeter-starves-the-core risk is structurally addressed but not yet proven. The two-engine model routes perimeter onto a non-senior engine; whether the platform leverage actually delivers ~4–5× on a regulated-adjacent book (vs a generic SOC-2 book) is a COI-capped vendor claim pending a pilot (R05 #5). Until the pilot returns, the perimeter is approved-but-gated, not approved-and-scaled. → Round 9 (the perimeter-leverage pilot) and Round 8 (the platform partner-vs-threat exchange).
  • P1 — the retainer reconciliation holds only for value-metered, earned-into renewals. If the firm drifts toward selling open-ended retainers cold to hit revenue, P1's resistance returns and the fast channel sours. → Round 6 (price the retainer on a defensible recurring value) and Round 7 (the sell motion must land the productized front door first).
  • P2 — the bank-side core is senior-heavy and earned, not led. C3/C4 cannot be leveraged down without breaching P2's documentation standard, and they push toward the 3–6 deep-client end of the ceiling; the bank ladder is therefore the firm's slowest-scaling, most senior-constrained track. → Round 9 (the senior-hire/pedigree plan; the bank track's capacity sequencing).
  • P8 — pricing POINTS are deferred and sit on a COI-capped Medium band. This round fixed packaging structure and value metrics; the actual numbers and the premium over single-regime/platform alternatives are Round 6's, gated on the buyer pricing probe (R03 #1). → Round 6.

Validation triggers (Round 5 — no new triggers; existing ones re-bound to packaging)

Round 5 introduces no new validation triggers — the honest outcome, since packaging is an architecture decision built on already-accepted research. It re-binds the existing triggers to the catalog:

  • T2 — bridge-core size (Critical × Low). Now binds D14/D15/D16: is the bridge core big enough to fill the senior books the per-advisor model and the expansion ladder assume? The double-edged-smallness fork. Closed by R01's buyer-side adoption/ACV data + the buyer-probe family.
  • T4 — dual-regime senior talent (Critical × Low). Now binds D16: can the layered pod's senior layer be staffed and benched? The moat-is-bottleneck gate (R05 C). Closed by the dual-regime talent census (R05 #2).
  • T1 / T5 (Critical × Low). Bind D14: is the bridge band wanted (T1) and bought as advisory vs self-served tooling (T5)? Closed by the buyer demand/advisory-conversion probe.
  • R03 #1 — buyer WTP / premium over single-regime/platform (Critical × Low). Binds D15's pricing structure and Round 6's points. Closed by the buyer pricing probe.
  • R03 #2 / R05 #1 — WNW's real renewal / NRR / utilization / senior-hours-per-engagement (Critical × Low). Binds D15's LTV assumptions and D16's capacity ceiling. Closed by the WNW internal data pull (one pull closes both, per R03/R05).
  • R05 #5 — realized platform leverage on a regulated book (Medium, pilot-gated). Binds D16's perimeter engine. Closed by the delivery pilot.

All sit in the same buyer-probe / internal-data family flagged since R01–R05: one buyer engagement plus one WNW internal data pull can close most of the set together.

Moderator's quality note (intervention check)

No defect logged. Personas stayed distinct and argued from their own priors: P1 pressed the productized, finish-lined, anti-open-retainer case and conceded only the value-metered, earned-into renewal; P2 held the documented, examiner-legible, SR-24-2 standard and conceded only to a bounded bank-side front door that ladders into the heavy retainer; P8 engineered the land-and-expand ladder and the two segment-specific value metrics and conceded the ladder is capacity-rationed; P3 grounded every line item in the layered pod and the who-delivers-at-what-utilization test; P11 held the economic floor, applied the two-variable knife-edge as a veto, pilot-gated the perimeter, and kept the smallness fork open. Genuine disagreement was forced along the two real fault lines (P1-productized vs P2-documented; P8-expansion vs P3/P11-staffability) and reconciled by structure, not by averaging — two package families off one delivery spine, and productization as the instrument that serves pricing, delivery, and margin at once.

With no Skeptic on this roster, P11 carried the adversarial economic role and took the last challenge before each decision (the engine-and-senior-hour-cost veto), and the Moderator kept P12's two carried tensions explicitly live and re-bound to the decisions: the double-edged-smallness / bridge-core-size fork (gated T2, carried into D14/D15/D16 and the dissent register) and the perimeter-starves-the-core risk (structurally addressed by the two-engine model, but pilot-gated on R05 #5, not waved through). Every market claim is grounded in an accepted research file (R01/R02/R03/R05/R07) or the brief at its own confidence, or carried as an explicit risk-weighted validation trigger. Pricing points were deliberately deferred to Round 6 and no number was committed, honoring the round boundary. No moderator-interventions.md entry created (no defect across R00–R05; the file is still not created).
