Risk weight: the flywheel mechanism rests on accepted R04 C + R05 D14 + R07 §B (Medium). The content-to-conversion rate is Critical × Medium (R04 B/#2) — built provisionally, instrumented, with a kill-criterion. Skeptic: accepted on exactly that condition.

D24 — The GTM economics view: the smallness fork answered as far as desk evidence allows, carried where it cannot — with a volume instrumentation-and-fallback structure

R06 D20 handed Round 7 the central pressure test: does the motion generate the volume to fill the senior books the per-advisor pricing assumes? The honest decision, reached with P12's last word:

  • What can be concluded: the motion is architected to maximize volume extraction from a narrow wedge. It is multi-engine (not dependent on any single channel that could fail or reprice), anchored on the highest-intent event in the market (the bridge trigger), and capacity-cheap (borrowed + referral + distributed content originate with low senior-hour cost per conversation, R05 D), so the supply-bound firm can run more pipeline per available founder hour than a senior-hour-intensive outbound motion could. Under R05's LTV:CAC (~7–20×, clears 3:1 with room), the firm does not break on demand-per-client, CAC, or LTV; it breaks only if total qualified volume is too thin to fill two-plus senior calendars at target utilization.
  • What cannot be concluded on desk evidence: whether the bridge-subset is large enough (T2) and whether niche demand converts to billable advisory at the needed rate (T1/T5) — i.e. whether the volume actually exists. Premium pricing cannot rescue an under-filled book (R06 D20). This is not closable without buyer/origination data and is not smoothed.
  • The fork stays OPEN, carried as T2, with an explicit structure the synthesis and Round 9 inherit: 1. Instrument volume from week one — qualified bridge-trigger conversations/month, per-channel origination yield, time-to-land, and senior-hours-per-land (the binding currency). This is the same origination-audit / buyer-probe family signed across R01–R05 (R04 #1, R05 #1); one internal pull + one buyer engagement closes most of it. 2. Define the under-fill kill/pivot criterion — if qualified volume does not trend toward filling the senior bench within the Phase-1 window, the response is not to drop the premium (which would forfeit the wedge, R06) but to widen the wedge in a controlled, halo-preserving direction (adjacent dual-regime triggers, the Canadian Streamlined cohort earlier, or a measured perimeter-engine expansion that does not become the visible identity, R05 D13 / R07 §D) — explicitly before abandoning the per-advisor model. 3. Carry the fork as the load-bearing validation trigger of the entire plan — the one number that decides whether the wedge is a business or a beautiful niche too small to fill.

Risk weight: the economics structure rests on accepted R05/R06 (Medium). The volume conclusion is Critical × Low until T1/T2 return — written as the plan's primary VALIDATION TRIGGER, per the standard's Critical×Low cell. Skeptic: the motion is sound conditional on a number not yet held; the plan must say so, instrument it from week one, and define the under-fill pivot — which D24 does.

Dissent that remains (carried, not resolved)

  • P5 vs P9 — owned vs borrowed origination: reconciled for now by sequence and senior-hour cost (borrow first, own in parallel), not settled in proportion. The actual owned-vs-borrowed mix is decided by the instrumentation (R04 #1/#2) — if content under-converts, the mix tilts permanently to partner+referral and the firm carries the pipeline-tenant risk P5 warned of. Live through Round 8 (partner terms) and Round 9 (instrumentation).
  • P1 vs P2 — channel pace: reconciled by R02 D6 sequence (SaaS-fast ACCESS leads, bank-slow QUALITY earned in), but P1's warning is live: if the regulated anchor makes the SaaS-fast motion slow/heavy, it breaks its own access channel (the F8/Medium tension, R04 carry). Instrument whether the regulated anchor suppresses SaaS-fast origination (Round 9).
  • P2's halo condition: the visible identity must stay regulated/judgment-led even as the perimeter engine does commodity work for cash (R07 §D; R04 D10) — a standing constraint on every channel and content asset, not a one-time decision.
  • P3's founder-time veto: the motion holds only if it pencils at the senior-hours the firm actually has after delivery — the protected founder content-block and the non-founder funnel handoff (Phase 2) are the mechanisms; if they slip, origination collapses back onto the founders and the firm stalls at founder-calendar scale. Live through Round 9.
  • P7's Canada-timing dissent (carried from R02): US-first may forfeit the freshest-now Canadian first-mover window; gated on T6, revisited Round 8 (CCUA/CBA channels).
  • P12's smallness fork: OPEN (D24) — the load-bearing trigger of the plan.

Open items and validation triggers

No new validation triggers introduced (the honest outcome, consistent with R05/R06 — the motion is built on accepted R04/R05/R07/R02 + the brief). Round 7 re-binds the existing triggers to GTM decisions:

  • R04 #1 (WNW origination audit — true first-touch source + time-to-close for the last ~10–20 clients/segment) now binds D21 (which engine actually originates), D22 (per-segment channel yield), and D24 (volume). The single input that lifts the channel map from Medium to High. Same internal-pull family as R05 #1.
  • R04 #2 (instrument the content engine — inbound-attributed pipeline, content-influenced win rate) binds D21/D23 — the content leg's kill-criterion. Critical × Medium inference until it returns.
  • R04 #4 (per-segment referral volume through the named venues — FS-ISAC/CB-ISAC/associations + partner-originated yield) binds D22 and the partner-detection argument; folded into the origination audit and into R08.
  • T1 (intersection/bridge demand) and T2 (bridge-core size / the smallness fork) bind D24 — the volume question; the load-bearing pair.
  • T5 (advisory-vs-tooling conversion) binds D24 — does niche demand convert to billable advisory or self-serve tooling.
  • T6 (Streamlined-Framework cohort velocity) binds D22's Canada-timing decision and the second origination wave.
  • T7 (frame recognition / message resonance) binds D22/D23 — copy must be tested on the bridge buyer's own frame before commitment; same buyer-probe family.

All sit in the same buyer-probe / internal-data family signed across R01–R05: one buyer engagement + one internal origination pull closes the load-bearing set (volume, origination mix, content conversion, frame resonance) together.

Carry-forward to Round 8 (partnerships — the immediate next unit)

  • The channel plan (D22) makes the partner exchange load-bearing, not optional: partners are the day-one origination engine (P9) and the only reliable detector of the low-observability bridge trigger. Round 8 must decide the actual exchange that makes each partner type send deals — auditors/C3PAOs, CPA firms (SaaS side), GRC-platform partner programs (SaaS side, the R02 double-edge to manage), cyber-insurers/brokers and fractional networks (both sides) — and the bank-side peer/association presence (FS-ISAC/CB-ISAC, ABA/ICBA/CCUA/CBA).
  • The GRC-platform double edge (R02): co-sell pipeline + up-market competitor + perimeter-engine leverage dependency (R05 #5) — Round 8 works the partner-vs-threat exchange.
  • Borrowed pipeline must convert to owned proof (P9's own concession): every partner-originated land must produce a reference + a content artifact (the flywheel) so the firm is not a permanent pipeline tenant. Round 8's exchanges should be structured to allow that.
  • R08 (partnerships research file) remains pending — commission it as Round 8's research-fill input if a Critical partnership decision would otherwise sit under-grounded; R04 F + R07 §B carried Round 7's channel-level decision without it.

Moderator's note on round quality

No defect. The five personas stayed distinct (P5 owned-engine/manufactured-referability; P9 borrowed-pipeline + the novel bridge-trigger-detection argument; P3 senior-hours-as-currency + the founder-time veto + productized-front-door-as-scalability; P1 fast-digital/finish-lined/frame-in-buyer's-words; P2 earned-slow/documented/halo-protection). Disagreement was forced along the two real fault lines (P5-vs-P9 origination energy; P1-vs-P2 channel pace) and reconciled by structure and sequence, not by averaging — borrowed-then-owned on senior-hour cost; SaaS-fast-then-bank-earned on R02 D6. P12 was seated per the ledger's next_unit and Rule 4, steelmanned the content-is-vanity case and the smallness fork to their strongest form, and took the last word before each decision; its conditions are recorded as binding (content as metered experiment with a kill-criterion; the smallness fork left explicitly OPEN as the plan's load-bearing trigger). Every channel claim is grounded in accepted research or labelled an inference with a risk weight; no market claim was waved through unsourced. The one place the round could not produce certainty — the volume question — is carried honestly as Critical × Low rather than smoothed, which is the correct treatment under the standard. moderator-interventions.md remains uncreated (no defect across R00–R07).

Round 8 · tier 3 · transcript
← back to the weave

Round 8 — Partnerships and Ecosystem

Phase: ROUNDS · Date: 2026-06-27 · Moderator-chaired

Convened (per MODERATOR.md Round 8 roster): P9 Partnerships & Ecosystem Builder · P6 Competitive & Market Analyst · P5 GTM & Demand Engine Lead · P10 Trust & Buyer-Psychology Expert. No Skeptic on this roster. Per Rule 4 the strongest adversarial voice on the roster — P6 — is given the last challenge before each decision is recorded. P12's two live dissents (owned-vs-borrowed mix; the smallness fork) are kept explicitly in view; they are not strawmanned.

Load-bearing inputs: R08 (08-partnerships.md, accepted — the five-currency exchange map) · R02 (GRC double-edge, encroachment speed) · R04 (positioning: halo, proof-before-claim, regulated anchor) · R05 (supply-bound; senior hours are the currency) · R07 (D21 borrowed-pipeline-led launch; D22 channel plan; the bridge-trigger-detection finding; D23 manufactured-referability flywheel).

What this round must decide (MODERATOR.md): the partnership plan and the exchange that makes each one work.

Framing the room (Moderator)

Round 7 did not leave partnerships as one option among several. D22 + the bridge-trigger-detection finding made the partner exchange load-bearing: partners are WNW's day-one origination engine and — because the bridge trigger (a SaaS vendor's FI deal stalling on security diligence) is high-intent but low-observability, visible to only four parties, three of which are partners — the only reliable detector of the firm's single highest-value event. R08 was then commissioned and accepted to ground the mechanism. Its decisive finding governs this round:

The exchanges are not one kind of thing. They sort into five structurally different currencies, and only one (auditor independence) is a forced referral that needs no incentive. Conflating them into a single "partner program" is the trap.

So the room does not debate "should we do partnerships" (settled in R07) or "what are the categories" (settled in the brief and R08). It debates, per leg: what is the actual exchange, is the lead worth anything when it arrives, and does building it cost more senior hours than it returns. P9 builds the case for each; P6 stress-tests each partner as also a competitor/commoditizer; P10 tests whether the partner's trust actually transfers or degrades under commercial load (R07 §D); P5 guards the owned-vs-borrowed energy budget (R07 D21 dissent, still live).

The opening analytic move — a SECOND axis on top of R08's five currencies (P10, sharpened by the room)

P10: R08 tells us what WNW gives in each exchange (the currency). It does not yet tell us what WNW gets — specifically, how warm the lead is when it lands, i.e. whether the partner's trust actually transfers to WNW or the buyer treats the introduction as a paid commercial list. That second thing decides how much re-earning WNW's own delivery has to do after the handoff, and it is not the same across legs. R07 §A/§B is the basis: buyers find firms by asking a person they trust (Hinge: 71% find firms by asking; ~79% of CISOs trust peers most), and trust-transfer (halo) degrades under excessive commercial load (R07 §D, the evidentiary basis for R04's halo condition). A referral is a trust-transfer event — but only when the buyer experiences it as "someone I trust vouched," not "a vendor I pay handed me a list."

P10's two-axis claim (adopted by the room as the round's key frame): cross R08's currency axis (what WNW gives) with a trust-transfer-strength axis (how warm the lead arrives, and whether the partner's credibility actually rubs off). The currency tells you the price of admission; the trust-transfer strength tells you what the lead is worth and how much delivery must re-earn.

Leg Currency (what WNW gives) Trust-transfer strength (what the lead is worth on arrival) Senior-hours to cultivate Sees the bridge trigger?
B — Auditor / C3PAO / CPA Nothing — independence forces the referral (R08 B) HIGH — buyer asked the auditor whom to trust; auditor stakes professional judgment Low–Med (relationship, not payment) Yes (mid-attestation)
D — Bank assn / ISAC Vetted member-benefit + royalty (R08 D) HIGH but SLOW — the seal is trust-transfer-at-scale; 6–9mo, prestige-gated High (vetting + cultivation) Indirectly (member CISOs)
C — Insurer / broker Gap-fill remediation so the policy binds (R08 C) MEDIUM — deadline-driven, transactional; "trust" is the broker's, thinly Low–Med Yes (renewal)
A — GRC platform Human delivery that closes the platform's deals (R08 A) LOW — buyer knows it's a paid service-partner roster; commercial load is high Low (program sign-up) Yes (mid-implementation)
E — Fractional network Referral fee / reciprocal capacity (R08 E, F) LOW–N/A — buyer often never sees the network; it's a work-routing relationship Low No

Moderator note (why this matters): the two-axis read changes the use of each leg, not just its rank. A high-volume / low-trust-transfer leg (platform) is a lead-volume faucet that must be re-earned by delivery, never an identity asset. A low-volume / high-trust-transfer leg (auditor, association) is an identity-and-credibility asset that builds the regulated halo R04 protects. Treating the platform lead as if it carried auditor-grade trust would be the error; so would dismissing the platform faucet because its trust is thin. The plan must route each leg to the job its two coordinates fit.

P6 (first adversarial pass, before any decision): I accept the second axis — it is the right correction — but I will hold the room to its consequence. Three of these five "partners" (A platform, C insurer-as-it-moves-up, E fractional network) are also commoditizers or competitors of exactly the work WNW sells. A trust-transfer score doesn't neutralize that. The currency frame plus the trust frame still misses a third coordinate I will press on every leg: does this partner, by sending WNW deals today, get stronger at replacing WNW tomorrow? Hold that.

Moderator: Recorded as P6's standing test — the encroachment coordinate (R02#3, encroachment speed into the $8–22K/mo band). It governs the platform decision below specifically. Now the decisions.

DECISION D25 — The partnership portfolio is a TIERED PORTFOLIO of five currencies, not a uniform program

The claim (P9, seconded by the room): WNW runs five distinct exchanges with five distinct designs, tiered by the two-axis read (D25 frame), sequenced by senior-hour cost and by R02-D6's access-then-quality logic. There is no single "WNW Partner Program" page, no uniform referral fee, no one-size partner agreement — each of those would mis-price four of the five legs.

The tiering (decided):

  • Tier 1 — the SPINE: Auditor / C3PAO / CPA (leg B). Highest trust-transfer, regulation-forced (no incentive to engineer), fee-free, durable (R08 B; AICPA independence is tightening, not eroding — Journal of Accountancy, Apr 2026, Primary, Medium·Supporting), SaaS-side, and a bridge-trigger detector (mid-attestation). This is the day-one origination spine on the SaaS side. [Decision rests on: R08 B — Fact·Primary(relayed)·High on the rule·Critical·Build; behavior = Medium, see trigger]
  • Tier 1 — the VOLUME FAUCET (quarantined): GRC platform (leg A). Fastest, lowest-cultivation-cost lead volume, but lowest trust-transfer and highest encroachment risk. Run it as a lead faucet that delivery re-earns, capped and quarantined (see D26-A and D27). [R08 A — Vendor·Medium·Supporting; double-edge Critical→flag]
  • Tier 2 — the BOTH-SIDES DEADLINE LAND: Insurer / broker (leg C). Medium trust-transfer, hard dated trigger (renewal), touches both ICPs, bridge-trigger detector. A productized readiness-review land. [R08 C — Secondary·Low–Medium·Supporting]
  • Tier 2 — the SLOW BANK-SIDE QUALITY CHANNEL: association / ISAC (leg D). High trust-transfer but slow and prestige-gated; the bank-channel entry ticket earned second per R02-D6. Sequenced, not launched cold (see D28). [R08 D — Primary(ABA/ICBA/state)·Medium·Supporting]
  • Tier 3 — SUPPLY + OVERFLOW: fractional network (leg E). Dual role: a marginal relief on the R05 supply ceiling and overflow origination. Lowest strategic weight; opportunistic. [R08 E — Secondary/Vendor·Low–Medium·Supporting]

The disagreement (forced — P5 vs P9, the live R07-D21 fault line):

P5: I will not let "five exchanges, tiered" become "pour the GTM energy into partners and call it a strategy." R07 D21 reconciled owned-vs-borrowed by sequence and senior-hour cost, not by surrender. Two of these legs (B auditor, D association) are cultivated, and cultivation is senior-hour-expensive — a managing-partner having coffee with C3PAOs and sitting on an ICBA committee is the same scarce senior hour R05 says is the binding constraint and R07 says is stolen from delivery. A partner portfolio that consumes 30% of founder time to originate is not "borrowed pipeline ≈0 hrs/lead"; it's a second full-time job. My condition: the portfolio is ranked by senior-hours-to-cultivate-per-qualified-lead, and the owned content engine (R07 D23) runs in parallel from week one, not after.

P9: Conceded on cost-accounting — and it sharpens the tiering, it doesn't refute it. That's exactly why leg B is the spine: the auditor referral is forced by independence (R08 B), so once the relationship exists the referral needs no ongoing senior selling — the lowest marginal-senior-hour origination in the entire R07 ranking. And it's why leg A (platform) is Tier 1 despite low trust — program sign-up is near-zero senior hours. The expensive legs (D association cultivation, deep auditor relationship-building) are explicitly Tier 2/slow. So the tiering already encodes your currency. Where I hold firm: borrowed pipeline isn't a substitute for the owned engine — it's the thing that fills the calendar while the owned engine compounds, and it's the only thing that catches the bridge trigger in time (R07). Kill the partner portfolio and you don't get a purer owned-content firm; you get an empty Q1 and a missed trigger.

P10: Both are right and the two-axis frame settles the proportion question without averaging. The legs P5 fears (B, D) are the high-trust-transfer legs — the ones whose senior-hour cost buys an identity asset, not just a lead. The legs that are cheap to cultivate (A platform) are low-trust — pure volume that delivery must re-earn. So the senior-hour spend is self-rationing: you spend founder hours only where the trust actually transfers (B, D), and you spend near-zero hours on the low-trust faucet (A). The portfolio is already shaped by trust-transfer ROI.

P6 (last challenge before D25): Fine — but name the failure mode you're tiering toward, not just away from. The seductive error here is not "too much energy on partners." It's building the whole origination on legs you don't control. Leg B's referral is forced by a rule WNW doesn't own — if AICPA softened tomorrow (it's tightening, so unlikely, but it's not WNW's rule), the spine bends. Leg A's faucet is owned by your up-market competitor. Leg D's seal is gated by an association that may judge you too small (R08 D). Leg C depends on brokers actually referring, which R08 says is unproven behavior. So I'll accept D25's tiering on one recorded condition: the portfolio is explicitly framed as borrowed-and-converted, with R07-D23's owned engine as the thing being built underneath it — partnerships buy time and triggers, they do not buy a moat. The moat is the dual-regime judgment + earned references (R03/R04), and every partner lead must be made to deposit into that moat (D27). With that condition, I don't object.

D25 — DECIDED: The partnership plan is a tiered portfolio of five structurally distinct exchanges, designed per leg, ranked on two axes (currency given × trust-transfer received) and a third encroachment coordinate (P6). Tier 1: auditor/CPA spine (B) + quarantined platform volume faucet (A). Tier 2: insurer/broker both-sides deadline land (C) + slow bank-side association channel (D). Tier 3: fractional supply/overflow (E). The owned expertise-led engine (R07 D23) runs in parallel from week one; partnerships are borrowed-and-converted, not a moat. Senior-hour spend is rationed to the high-trust-transfer legs. Rests on: R08 (whole) · R07 D21/D22/D23 · R02-D6 sequence. Confidence: Medium (mechanism grounded; realized referral behavior is the open trigger). Carried condition (P6): partnerships buy time and triggers, not a moat.

DECISION D26 — The exchange, per leg (the core output)

For each leg: what WNW gives · what the partner gets · the mechanism that makes them send deals · the cash/term structure · the bridge-trigger handoff. All five are decided below. Three of the four high-value legs (A, C, D) are the parties who see the bridge trigger (R08 G), so each carries an explicit trigger-detection handoff.

D26-A — GRC platform (Vanta, Drata): co-sell pipeline, quarantined

  • WNW gives: the human delivery layer (readiness, vCISO judgment, gap remediation) the platform's software cannot deliver but its customers need — i.e. WNW closes the platform's own deals and reduces its churn. [R08 A · Vendor · Medium]
  • Partner gets: a service partner that makes its platform "sticky" (customers who get to attestation renew the software).
  • Mechanism: join the service/MSP partner programs (Vanta Service Partner; Drata Alliance "Channel/Service" lane) — both documented as no-cost, no-commitment sign-up with co-sell resources, partner demo instances, and co-marketing (R08 A). Get listed in the service directory where the platform's customers shop for delivery help.
  • Cash/term: platform co-sell economics are not publicly priced (R08 A, COI flag) — Supporting×Low trigger; do not assume margin. The visible numbers ($500 Vanta customer-referral bounty; ~20–25% Drata end-customer discount) are not the service-partner economics and are not WNW's lever.
  • Bridge-trigger handoff: the platform sees customers mid-implementation who stall on a buyer's diligence — instrument a "flag the stalled-diligence customer to WNW" path with partner CSMs. This is the platform's specific trigger-detection value.
  • The quarantine (P6's double-edge, made operational): multi-platform, never single-platform; treat every platform lead as low-trust volume that delivery re-earns (D25 frame); and bind it to D27 — every platform-routed land must manufacture an owned reference + content artifact, or WNW becomes a permanent pipeline tenant of its own up-market competitor (R02; R07 D23). Never position the firm's identity on platform partnership (R04 halo / D10 exclusion — commodity SaaS visibility collapses the halo).

P6: This is the leg I most distrust and I'll say why precisely: the platform is the one partner whose product roadmap is to eat your service. Cynomi raised a $37M Series B to do AI vCISO (R02); the platforms move up-market into the retainer band (R02#3 encroachment speed). When you co-sell with them you are training your replacement and handing it your client list. P9: Which is the argument for the quarantine, not against the leg — the volume is real and near-free to access, and the defense is structural: cap dependency (multi-platform), and convert every land to an owned asset so the relationship with the client is WNW's, not the platform's. The platform owns the system-of-record; WNW must own the judgment relationship and the reference. P6 (last challenge, D26-A): Accept — with the dependency cap as a hard rule, not a preference: no single platform may originate more than a stated share of pipeline (set the threshold in Round 9 instrumentation), and the day a platform's own delivery arm competes for a renewal, that leg is reclassified from partner to competitor. Recorded.

D26-B — Auditor / C3PAO / CPA: the regulation-forced spine

  • WNW gives: clean, audit-ready clients (the auditor's attestation runs smoothly) and a trusted prep partner the auditor can name without violating independence. WNW gives no fee — and must not, or it risks tainting the independence the referral rests on.
  • Partner gets: independence preserved (AICPA bars the attestor from doing the prep — "the CPA firm attests, the consultant prepares, the MSSP operates," R08 B, Primary, High on the rule), clients who arrive ready (less audit friction), and a reciprocal referral back (WNW's readiness clients need an attestor).
  • Mechanism: build reciprocal handoff relationships with C3PAOs and SOC-attesting CPA firms — readiness → attestation one way, attestation-needed → trusted auditor the other. The motive is structural and standing: the auditor is professionally prohibited from doing the prep and wants the client ready (R08 B). No incentive engineering required.
  • Cash/term: none — this is the non-cash leg (R08 F). A referral fee would be counterproductive (independence optics). The exchange is reciprocity + clean clients.
  • Bridge-trigger handoff: the auditor sees the SaaS vendor exactly when an FI buyer's diligence demands attestation it doesn't yet have — the highest-fidelity bridge-trigger sighting on the SaaS side. Build the relationship so the auditor routes the not-yet-ready deal-blocked vendor to WNW's Bridge Engagement (R05 D14).

P10: This is the leg where trust-transfer is strongest and cleanest, and here's the mechanism: the buyer asked the auditor whom to trust, and the auditor — who can't take the work — names WNW. The buyer experiences that as expert peer guidance, not a paid handoff (there's no fee to taint it). That is the single warmest lead in the portfolio. P9: And the most durable — it's the only one backed by a rule that is tightening (R08 B; Journal of Accountancy Apr 2026). Make it the spine. P6 (last challenge, D26-B): My only challenge is the one R08 already flagged and I won't let the room round it up: the motive is High (independence is real), but the behavior — do auditors refer to WNW specifically rather than to a generic shortlist of three readiness shops — is unproven (R08 trigger, Critical×Low). The spine is structurally sound; whether WNW becomes the named referral depends on the operator-pedigree and same-industry-proof assets from R07 §B (the auditor vouches for whom the auditor trusts). So: build the spine, but the validation trigger rides on it and the proof assets (R04/R07) are the thing that converts "a list" into "WNW." Recorded — no objection to the spine.

D26-C — Insurer / broker: the both-sides deadline land

  • WNW gives: pre-binding/pre-renewal remediation so a client who would fail underwriting can pass it — the policy binds, the broker keeps the commission and the client.
  • Partner gets: bound policies (revenue) and retained clients they'd otherwise lose to a declined application; the insurer's risk-engineering function gets reduced loss ratios.
  • Mechanism: productize a "Cyber Insurance Readiness Review" (fixed-scope, ~2–3 weeks; R08 C cites a ~$1,500–$3,000 vendor band — illustrative only, COI/Low) as the referral artifact brokers/MGAs can hand to a failing applicant. Underwriting is now evidence-based (carriers verify MFA/EDR/backups before binding; deny on gaps — R08 C, Secondary, Medium), so the gap is real and dated (renewal).
  • Cash/term: where a fee applies, the PS benchmark is 10% most common / 5% second, 12-mo cap (R08 F, Secondary, Medium). Many broker referrals run fee-free (the broker's incentive is the bound policy, not a kickback).
  • Bridge-trigger handoff: the broker sees the client at renewal — a hard, dated, both-sides trigger. Instrument a "failing-underwriting → WNW readiness review" referral path.
  • Both-sides note: this is the one leg that touches both ICPs (SaaS vendors and small FIs) at the same event (renewal). The readiness review is a low-priced land, not the core — its job is to open the relationship that ladders into C1/C2 or C3/C4 (R05 D15).

P10: Trust-transfer here is medium and I want the room honest about why: the broker isn't staking deep professional judgment the way the auditor is — the broker is solving a deadline. The lead arrives warm-ish but transactional. Treat the readiness review as a relationship-opener that delivery must convert, not as a trust windfall. P6 (last challenge, D26-C): The behavior risk here is the worst of any leg — R08 says brokers "optimize for getting the policy renewed, not for the client passing," which cuts both ways: it's the opening (they don't remediate themselves) and the risk (they may just push the client to a more lenient carrier rather than refer remediation). So the broker-referral behavior is the least proven in the set (R08 C caveat). Decision: build leg C as a Tier-2 productized land, gate it on the same referral-behavior trigger as leg B, and do not let the small readiness-review fee define the relationship — it's a foot in the door for the ladder. Recorded.

D26-D — Bank association / ISAC: the slow trust-transfer channel (sequenced in D28)

  • WNW gives: a vetted, member-benefiting offering (discount/dividend/education per ICBA PSP requirement, R08 D) and, for paid programs, a royalty.
  • Partner gets: a credible solution for members + royalty revenue (ABA Endorsed Solutions runs through the for-profit Corporation for American Banking; ICBA PSP requires a member benefit — R08 D, Primary, Medium).
  • Mechanism: endorsement / trust-transfer at scale — the seal is the bank-channel entry ticket (same-industry credibility a peer recognizes, R07 §B). Precedent is established: security/risk advisory IS an endorsable category (ICBA named Finosec for cybersecurity governance; Ncontracts for vendor/risk/compliance — R08 D, Primary).
  • Cash/term: royalty/member-benefit, not a per-deal referral fee; economics are undisclosed (R08 D, single-origin gap → Supporting×Low trigger).
  • Bridge-trigger handoff: indirect — association/ISAC presence puts WNW next to member CISOs (FS-ISAC is presence/sponsorship, not endorsement — its Critical Providers Program is for hyperscalers, not boutiques, R08 D).
  • Full sequencing decided in D28.

D26-E — Fractional network: supply + overflow

  • WNW gives / gets: a referral fee on placed overflow work (10%/5%, R08 F) and/or reciprocal capacity — access to scarce senior dual-regime practitioners without permanent payroll (marginal relief on the R05 supply ceiling).
  • Mechanism: join vCISO marketplaces/networks as both a supply node (take overflow the network can't place) and an occasional capacity source (R08 E, Low–Medium).
  • Trust-transfer: low/N-A — the buyer typically never sees the network; it's a work-routing relationship. Keep it opportunistic, Tier 3.
  • P3 lens (borrowed for E, the supply role): quality control is the constraint — the dual-regime senior sliver is web-unmeasured (R05/T4); vetting any network-sourced senior to WNW's bar is non-negotiable, or the halo (R04) takes commodity damage.

P6 (last challenge before D26 as a whole): I'll register the one cross-leg risk the table format hides. Four of these five exchanges (A, B, C, E — all but the association seal) deliver a lead, not a commitment — and a lead from a partner whose own incentive is something other than WNW's success (platform wants stickiness, broker wants the bound policy, network wants its fee). Only leg B's incentive (independence) is structurally aligned with sending WNW good work it can't poach. So the portfolio's quality, not just its volume, is concentrated in the spine. Decision stands, but it underscores D25's tiering: the spine carries the quality; the rest carry volume that delivery must qualify and re-earn.

D26 — DECIDED: the five exchanges are designed as above — each with its give/get/mechanism/cash-term/trigger-handoff specified. The spine (B) is fee-free and structurally aligned; the platform (A) is quarantined volume; the broker (C) is a both-sides deadline land; the association (D) is slow trust, sequenced in D28; the network (E) is opportunistic supply/overflow. Rests on: R08 A–F. Confidence: Medium on mechanisms; the realized referral behavior for B and C is the carried Critical×Low trigger; platform/association economics are the Supporting×Low trigger.

DECISION D27 — The anti-tenancy conversion architecture: every partner-originated land must DEPOSIT into the owned moat

The claim (P9's own R07-D23 concession, made a hard rule): borrowed pipeline that does not convert to owned proof makes WNW a permanent pipeline tenant with no pricing power. So every partner-originated engagement is structured, at point of sale, to manufacture an owned asset: (1) a reference (the same-industry / examiner-legible artifact from R05 D14's dual-artifact Bridge Engagement — the bank-channel entry ticket and the next buyer's peer proof), and (2) a content artifact (a wedge-scoped case the owned engine distributes, R07 D23). The partner originates the first conversation; WNW owns the relationship, the reference, and the next conversation.

Why this is the P5-vs-P9 reconciliation (not an average):

P5: This is the only version of the partner portfolio I'll endorse, and it's the resolution of the owned-vs-borrowed fight: partnerships stop being a substitute for owned demand and become a feeder of it. Each borrowed land deposits a reference + a content asset into the owned engine, so the flywheel (R07 D23) spins faster with partners, not instead of them. Borrowed pipeline that converts is owned-demand fuel; borrowed pipeline that doesn't is tenancy. The rule makes the difference operational.

P9: Agreed — and it's the answer to the platform double-edge too. The reason platform tenancy is dangerous is that the platform owns the system-of-record and the relationship. If WNW owns the reference and the judgment relationship, the platform owns only the tooling — and WNW can be found next time by the reference's peer network without the platform. Convert, and the dependency inverts over time.

P10: The trust mechanics make this non-optional, not just smart. The reference is the highest rung of the proof hierarchy that actually transfers (R07 §B: peer referral > same-industry refs > operator pedigree). A partner lead is borrowed trust; a reference is owned trust. Converting borrowed trust into owned proof is literally how a firm graduates from "on a partner's list" to "the name the peer recommends." Without D27, WNW never accumulates the asset that wins the deal without the partner.

P6 (last challenge, D27): Two conditions or the rule is theater. One: the conversion must be contractually/operationally enforced at scoping, not hoped for after delivery — a reference and a content artifact are deliverable line items of the engagement, with client consent secured up front (especially for the examiner-legible artifact, where the bank client will be reference-shy — R04 P2's documented-defensibility demand cuts against easy public references). Two: respect the halo (R04 / R07 §D) — a platform co-marketing case study is low-trust and must not become the firm's visible identity; the references that build identity are the auditor-spine and bank-side ones. Convert every land, but publish along the regulated/judgment axis, not the commodity-platform axis, or the conversion damages the very halo it's meant to feed. Recorded as binding.

D27 — DECIDED: every partner-originated engagement is structured at scoping to produce (1) an owned reference and (2) an owned content artifact, converting borrowed trust into owned proof and feeding the R07-D23 flywheel. This reconciles P5-vs-P9 by making partnerships a feeder of owned demand, not a substitute. Binding conditions (P6): conversion is a scoped deliverable with up-front consent; published proof stays on the regulated/judgment axis to protect the halo (R04 / R07 §D). Rests on: R07 D23 · R05 D14 · R04 D10/halo · R07 §B/§D. Confidence: Medium.

DECISION D28 — Bank-side sequencing: presence/sponsorship → state assn / ICBA PSP → national ABA later; protect the seal's credibility

The claim (P9 + P10, on R02-D6's access-then-quality logic): the bank-side trust channel (leg D) is earned second and sequenced from reachable to prestige, because the seals are slow (6–9 months), prestige-gated, and tilt national-scale — a WNW-scale boutique may be too small to win the top ABA seal early (R08 D, Primary, Medium):

  1. First (months 0–12): presence + sponsorship + peer access — FS-ISAC / CB-ISAC presence and sponsorship (presence, not endorsement — R08 D), state banking-association events, CCUA/CBA conferences (Canada — R08 source 13). Near-term, low-gate, builds the same-industry references that qualify WNW for endorsement later. Pairs with the R07 D22 bank channel (peer-CISO, association-gated).
  2. Second (months 9–24): state association endorsement + ICBA PSP path — the lower, reachable rung (R08 D: state programs vetted by association staff; ICBA PSP precedent proven for security/risk — Finosec, Ncontracts). Requires a member benefit (discount/dividend/education) and clears a vetting bar WNW can plausibly meet at boutique scale.
  3. Third (months 18+, scale-gated): national ABA Endorsed Solutions — pursue only when scale supports it (national reach, 6–9mo due diligence through the Corporation for American Banking). Not a launch move.

The P10 condition (trust-transfer under commercial load — R07 §D): the association seal is high-trust precisely because it reads as the association's judgment, not a paid placement. ABA Endorsed Solutions runs through a for-profit subsidiary (R08 D) — so the commercial load is already present and must be managed: the member benefit must be real (or the endorsement degrades into a vendor ad and stops transferring trust). WNW must earn the seal on substance (the dual-regime depth, R04) so the endorsement is credible, not bought. A seal the members read as "pay-to-play" transfers no trust.

The disagreement (P5 vs P9, scoped to timing):

P5: My only push here — don't let "earned second" become "ignored until year two." The presence/sponsorship rung is owned-engine-compatible and should start in month one in parallel with the SaaS spine; it's where the bank-side content (R07 D23) gets distributed and where the same-industry references get seen. The slow seal can wait; the peer presence cannot. P9: Agreed — presence is week-one, the seal is year-two; that's the sequence, not a deferral. P7's live Canada-timing dissent (carried, R02→R07): the freshest regulatory tailwind is Canadian (Streamlined Framework, launched ~25 Jun 2026); CCUA/CBA presence should not wait for the US seals — gated on T6, revisited in Round 9. Moderator: carried, not resolved here (it's a sequencing/timing call that rides on T6 cohort velocity).

P6 (last challenge, D28): The eligibility question is a fact gap, not a strategy choice, and I won't let the room assume the answer. Whether a WNW-scale boutique can win even the state/ICBA rung early is partly desk-answerable from program criteria and partly a program-conversation trigger (R08 D residual). So: sequence as decided, but treat boutique-eligibility for each rung as a check to run, not an assumption — and don't build any Critical bank-side origination forecast on a seal WNW hasn't confirmed it qualifies for. The reachable origination on the bank side in year one is presence + peer references, not the seal. Recorded.

D28 — DECIDED: bank-side leg D is sequenced presence/sponsorship (month 1, parallel) → state assn / ICBA PSP (months 9–24) → national ABA (18+, scale-gated). The member benefit must be substantive so the endorsement reads as the association's judgment, not paid placement (P10, R07 §D). Canada presence (CCUA/CBA) not deferred behind US seals (P7, gated T6). Eligibility per rung is a check to run, not an assumption (P6). Rests on: R08 D · R02-D6 · R07 §B/§D/D22. Confidence: Medium; boutique-eligibility = Supporting×Low trigger.

Validation triggers (re-bound; honest — no invented new ones)

Round 8 introduced no new validation triggers — the honest outcome, since the plan is built on accepted R08 + R02/R04/R05/R07. It re-binds R08's two carried triggers to specific decisions, and confirms they sit in the same partner/buyer-probe family the whole deliberation has been consolidating:

  • Partner referral-BEHAVIOR probe [Critical×Low → VALIDATION TRIGGER · NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL] (R08) — now binds D26-B and D26-C directly (and through them the Tier-1 spine and the Tier-2 deadline land). Desk established the motive (auditor independence; broker bound-policy incentive); the realized behavior — do auditors/C3PAOs and brokers refer out at volume, and to WNW specifically vs. a generic shortlist — is interview-dependent. → interview 5–10 auditors/C3PAOs + 3–5 cyber brokers/MGAs. Same probe family as T1 / R04#1 / R04#4 — one partner-interview pass closes referral behavior + per-channel yield together.
  • Private program economics [Supporting×Low → trigger] (R08) — binds D26-A (platform co-sell margin/lead-volume) and D26-D / D28 (association royalty + boutique scale-eligibility). Behind partner agreements; closed only by direct program conversations. The platform dependency cap (D26-A) and the eligibility-per-rung check (D28) are the operational hedges until it returns.
  • R09 (cyber-insurance) interface — confirmed not commissioned this round: R08 C established the broker referral mechanism, which is what leg C's exchange decision needed; R09's demand-driver corroboration (tracing 82% MFA-denial / 41% first-submission-denial to Coalition/Marsh/Munich Re primaries) is not required to ground D26-C's exchange. Commission R09 only if Round 9 or synthesis needs the insurer leg's demand basis (not its mechanism) at >Medium. Gate-checked: NO.

Re-bound prior triggers: R07 D21 owned-vs-borrowed mix → reconciled in proportion by D27 (borrowed feeds owned via mandatory conversion) but the realized mix is still instrumentation-decided (Round 9); R02#3 platform-encroachment-speed → binds D26-A's dependency cap + reclassification rule; T2 smallness fork → still live (partnerships address origination, not whether the wedge is big enough to fill senior books — that remains the plan's load-bearing trigger, R07 D24).

Carried dissent (still live after Round 8)

  • P5-vs-P9 owned-vs-borrowed MIX — reconciled in principle by D27 (convert every land), but the realized proportion (how much pipeline is partner-originated vs. owned-content-originated) is instrumentation-decided in Round 9, not settled here. If content under-converts, the mix tilts permanently to partners = the pipeline-tenant risk D27 guards against. Live.
  • P6 platform double-edge — accepted with the dependency cap + reclassification rule (D26-A); the threat is managed, not eliminated. The platform remains simultaneously channel and up-market competitor; encroachment speed (R02#3) is a Round 9 instrument.
  • P10 trust-transfer-under-commercial-load — the standing constraint on D27 (publish on the regulated axis) and D28 (substantive member benefit). A partner relationship over-commercialized stops transferring trust; the halo (R04) governs every published partner artifact.
  • P7 Canada-timing — CCUA/CBA presence not deferred behind US seals (D28), but the weight of the early Canada bet rides on T6 (Streamlined cohort velocity); revisited Round 9.
  • P12 smallness fork (carried, not in-room this round) — partnerships maximize origination from a narrow wedge but do not answer whether the bridge-core is big enough to fill 2+ senior calendars. Remains the plan's primary load-bearing validation trigger (R07 D24, Critical×Low until T1/T2 return).

Moderator quality note

No defect. Personas stayed distinct and argued from their own priors: P9 built each borrowed-pipeline case and conceded the conversion rule as its own (R07 D23); P6 ran the competitor/commoditizer and encroachment lens on every leg and held the last challenge before each decision (the Rule-4 adversarial seat, since no Skeptic is on the Round 8 roster); P10 supplied the second (trust-transfer) axis that became the round's key analytic frame and held the commercial-load condition; P5 guarded the owned-vs-borrowed energy budget and forced the senior-hour-cost accounting. Disagreement was forced along two real fault lines — P5-vs-P9 (owned vs borrowed origination energy, reconciled by D27's feeder structure, not averaged) and P9-vs-P6 (partner-as-channel vs partner-as-competitor, reconciled by D25's tiering + D26-A's quarantine, not averaged) — and P10's trust axis settled the proportion question without splitting the difference. Every market claim is grounded in an accepted research file (R08 primarily; R02/R04/R05/R07) or labelled with its risk weight. No new validation triggers were invented (honest outcome); R08's two carried triggers were re-bound to specific decisions. The one Critical input still open — partner referral behavior — is correctly carried as a signed NEEDS EXTERNAL RETRIEVAL trigger, not papered over. No moderator-interventions.md entry (file still not created across R00–R08).

Round 8 decisions, in one place

  • D25 — Partnership plan = a tiered portfolio of five distinct exchanges, ranked on currency-given × trust-transfer-received (+ encroachment coordinate), borrowed-and-converted (not a moat), with the owned engine running in parallel from week one. Tier 1: auditor spine (B) + quarantined platform faucet (A). Tier 2: broker deadline land (C) + slow association channel (D). Tier 3: fractional supply/overflow (E).
  • D26 — The exchange per leg, fully specified (give/get/mechanism/cash-term/bridge-trigger handoff): (A) platform co-sell, quarantined + dependency-capped; (B) auditor/CPA regulation-forced fee-free spine; (C) broker both-sides readiness-review land at renewal; (D) association endorsement, sequenced (D28); (E) fractional supply/overflow, opportunistic.
  • D27 — Anti-tenancy conversion architecture: every partner-originated land manufactures an owned reference + content artifact at scoping (consent up front; published on the regulated axis to protect the halo). Reconciles owned-vs-borrowed by making partners a feeder of owned demand.
  • D28 — Bank-side sequencing: presence/sponsorship (month 1, parallel) → state assn / ICBA PSP (9–24mo) → national ABA (18+, scale-gated); substantive member benefit so the seal transfers trust; Canada presence not deferred; eligibility per rung is a check to run.

Next unit: Round 9 — Execution architecture (rounds/round-09-execution.md). Personas per MODERATOR.md: Operator (P3), GTM Lead (P5), Capacity Modeler (P11), Pricing Architect (P8). Constructive only — milestones, success factors, KPIs/leading indicators, operating cadence, artifact list. The smallness-fork instrumentation (T2), the senior-hour ceiling (R05), the partner-channel instruments (D27 conversion rate, D26-A dependency cap, referral-behavior trigger), and the content-engine kill-criterion (R04#2) are Round 9's measurement set.

Round 9 · tier 3 · transcript
← back to the weave

Round 9 — Execution Architecture

Phase: ROUNDS · Date: 2026-06-27 · Moderator-chaired

Convened (per MODERATOR.md Round 9 roster): P3 Boutique Operator · P5 GTM & Demand Engine Lead · P11 Unit-Economics & Capacity Modeler · P8 Pricing & Packaging Architect. No Skeptic on this roster. Per Rule 4 the strongest adversarial voice on the roster — P11, who holds the economic floor and the veto — is given the last challenge before each decision is recorded. P12's standing dissent (the smallness fork) and P7's standing dissent (Canada timing) are kept explicitly in view; they are not strawmanned.

Load-bearing inputs (all accepted): R01 (supply-bound SOM ~$2–5M/yr) · R03 (value metrics; specialist premium; SPI/Deltek PS benchmarks — billable util 68.9%, rev/consultant $199K, logo retention 83–85%, mid-mkt NRR ~108%) · R05 (the decisive supply-bound finding; per-advisor model; vCISO bandwidth ceiling; loaded-CAC = senior selling time; platform leverage ~4–5× on the commodity layer only) · R07 (D21 three-phase founder-led→scalable motion; D23 manufactured-referability flywheel; D24 the smallness fork as the plan's load-bearing trigger; the content-engine kill-criterion) · R08/Round 8 (D26-A platform dependency cap + reclassify-on-compete; D27 borrowed→owned conversion; D28 bank-side sequencing; the referral-behavior trigger) · R06-pricing/Round 6 (D17–D20 committed bands; the COI cap = list-not-WTP; the effective-senior-rate-after-pod-leverage test).

What this round must decide (MODERATOR.md Round 9): the execution scaffolding — milestones, success factors, the KPI and leading-indicator set, the operating cadence, and the artifact list. Constructive only (Rule 10): this round carries milestones, conditions-that-must-hold, instruments, and assets-to-build. It does not carry failure points, risks, or attack surfaces — the red team that follows synthesis owns those. Where a strategic decision is gated on an unvalidated input, Round 9's job is to convert that gate into a day-one instrument with a pre-defined reading, not to author the way it could fail.

Framing the room (Moderator)

Eight rounds have produced a locked strategy: a dual-regime vendor-diligence specialist (R04 D9), wedged on the bridge buyer (D11), delivered as a two-engine catalog (R05 D13) priced on the specialization premium (R06 D17), originated by a three-phase borrowed-pipeline-led motion (R07 D21) feeding an owned manufactured-referability flywheel (D23), with a tiered five-currency partner portfolio (R08 D25) converting every borrowed land into owned proof (D27).

Round 9 does not re-open any of that. It builds the scaffolding to run it — and, critically, to measure the one thing the desk could not establish. Every prior round converged on the same residual: the plan is favorable on demand quality, retention, NRR, marketing-CAC, and LTV:CAC (R05 ~7–20×, clears the 3:1 bar); it breaks only on two binding constraints — senior-hour supply (R05: WNW is supply-bound) and qualified-volume demand from a narrow wedge (R07 D24: the smallness fork, Critical×Low until T1/T2 return). These two are not independent; the plan is viable precisely in the band where enough qualified volume arrives and enough senior hours exist to deliver it at premium realization.

So the Moderator frames Round 9 around a single discipline the room adopts as its governing frame:

Instrument the fork, not the dashboard. The execution plan's first job is to make the two binding constraints — and the one load-bearing unknown that sits at their intersection (does the bridge wedge generate enough qualified volume to fill 2+ senior calendars at premium prices?) — measurable early enough to act on, with the response pre-defined. Every other metric earns its place only if it changes a decision. A 30-metric vanity dashboard run by a two-person founding firm spends the same scarce senior hour that delivery needs (R05; R07 P3 founder-time veto). Measure what moves a lever; cut the rest.

P3 owns who-delivers-at-what-utilization and the operating cadence; P5 owns the origination instrumentation and the funnel; P8 owns price-integrity-in-the-field (realized vs list, scope-creep-as-silent-discount); P11 holds the economic floor, the per-advisor hypothesis, and the Rule-4 last challenge before each decision.

DECISION D29 — The execution roadmap: three phased milestone tracks on the R07-D21 motion, dated and owner-implied

The claim (P3, built on R07 D21's three-phase motion): execution sequences as three phases matching the R07 sales-motion phases, each with a milestone set across four tracks — Origination, Delivery/Capacity, Partner, Measurement — so that no phase advances until its load-bearing capability is standing. Month 0 = July 2026 (today is 2026-06-27).

Phase 1 — Founder-led, borrowed-pipeline-led (months 0–~9; Jul 2026 – ~Apr 2027)

Goal: stand up the productized front door, the auditor spine, the owned content engine, and the day-one instrumentation — and get the first reading on the fork.

  • Origination (owner: founder/managing partner): publish the wedge-scoped content spine in the buyer's frame from week one (R07 D23; not after — P5's parallel-from-day-one condition, R08 D25); productized fixed-fee front door live (C1 Bridge ~$30–45K / C3 ~$35–75K+, R06 D17) as the land; cold outbound not an engine (R07, 3–6% supplement only).
  • Delivery/Capacity (owner: founder + junior/analyst pod): the layered pod operational (senior=judgment, junior=commodity sub-tasks, platform=automatable layer — R05 D16); the perimeter-leverage pilot runs on a real regulated-adjacent book to prove ~4–5× platform leverage before P-1 scales (R05 #5 gate — D31 instruments it).
  • Partner (owner: founder): the auditor/C3PAO/CPA spine (R08 D26-B) cultivated first — reciprocal readiness↔attestation handoffs; presence/sponsorship rung on the bank side (FS-ISAC/CB-ISAC, state assns) and CCUA/CBA presence in Canada from month 1, not deferred (R08 D28; P7).
  • Measurement (owner: founder): the minimal instrument set (D31) live from first engagement — the first 2 quarters of real operating data is what closes the internal-data family (R05 #1 / R03 #1 / R04 #1) that the desk could not reach.
  • Phase-1 exit milestone: a first same-industry examiner-legible reference manufactured off a delivered Bridge Engagement (R05 D14 dual artifact) — the bank-channel entry ticket (R07 §B) — and a first fork reading against the under-fill criterion (D31).

Phase 2 — Non-founder funnel + first ceiling-lift (months ~9–24; ~Apr 2027 – ~Jul 2028)

Goal: take the top/middle funnel off the founder, lift the senior ceiling, open the bank-direct motion.

  • Origination: non-founder BD + junior pod run top/middle of the productized funnel (P3's scalability mechanism — the front door is productized precisely so a non-founder can run it, R07); the flywheel turning (references → peer proof → content → partner reasons-to-route, R07 D23).
  • Delivery/Capacity: the first senior dual-regime hire and/or apprenticeship under a senior — the only ceiling-lifter, since the senior layer does not leverage (R05 C / T4); ideally the hire arrives reference-bearing (ex-examiner/regulated-shop pedigree, R04→R09 hiring note; R07 §B operator-pedigree rung), which also re-opens R02's narrowed bank-first fork.
  • Partner: state association endorsement + ICBA PSP path (months 9–24, R08 D28; precedent: Finosec/Ncontracts); the Canada second wave on the Streamlined-Framework cohort (~12–18mo from the 25 Jun 2026 launch ≈ mid-2027–early 2028, gated T6 — P7's sequencing milestone).
  • Measurement: the per-advisor economics reconstructed against the pilot-hypothesis band with real data (D31), confirming or refuting R05's model; partner borrowed→owned conversion rate (D27) tracked per leg.
  • Phase-2 exit milestone: the funnel runs without founder origination hours on the SaaS side; ≥1 senior bench seat delivering at target utilization; a confirmed (or refuted-and-pivoted) read on the fork.

Phase 3 — Multi-engine compounding (months 24+; ~Jul 2028+)

Goal: founder reserved for senior delivery, closes, and cross-sell; the bank-direct motion compounding.

  • Origination/Partner: owned + semi-owned channels compounding; national ABA Endorsed Solutions pursued only when scale supports it (R08 D28, scale-gated — not a launch move).
  • Delivery/Capacity: the land→expand→cross-sell ladder (R05 D15) climbed capacity-sequenced — offer only the rungs the current senior bench delivers at target utilization (R05 D16); cross-border + both-sides axes = the richest cross-sell inventory and the capacity test.
  • Measurement: the validation-trigger register (D33) substantially closed by accumulated operating data; the fork answered.

The disagreement (forced — P5 vs P3/P11, on milestone load):

P5: I want Phase 1 to commit to a real origination build — per-channel attribution, content-influenced pipeline tracking, a properly instrumented funnel — because if we don't measure where the next ten clients come from, we're flying blind on the exact question the whole plan rides on (R07 D24). The fork is my question; under-build the origination instrumentation and we can't read it.

P3: And if you build a 30-metric attribution stack in month one, the founder is doing analytics instead of delivering the engagements that generate the references the whole flywheel needs. A two-person firm in Phase 1 has one scarce resource and it is the same senior hour that delivers, sells, and would run your dashboard (R05; R07 founder-time veto). The milestone isn't "rich instrumentation"; it's "the minimum instrument that reads the fork, run at a cadence a busy founder can actually sustain."

P11 (last challenge before D29): Both of you are circling the real constraint, so let me name it as the gate. The roadmap is sound only if every milestone is staffable at the senior-hours available after delivery — that's the R05 supply bound applied to the plan itself, not just to client work. So I'll accept D29 on one recorded condition: each Phase-1 milestone declares its senior-hour cost, exactly as R05 D16 made every catalog line declare its engine. The content block, the auditor cultivation, the perimeter pilot, and the instrumentation each steal from the same delivery calendar. If the four Phase-1 tracks together exceed the founder's non-delivery hours, the roadmap isn't aggressive — it's unstaffable, and it fails on the spreadsheet before it fails in the market. With per-milestone senior-hour accounting and P3's minimal instrument set (not P5's full stack until Phase 2 BD exists to run it), I don't object.

D29 — DECIDED: execution runs as three phases on the R07-D21 motion, each with milestones across four tracks (Origination, Delivery/Capacity, Partner, Measurement), dated from month 0 = Jul 2026, owners implied per track. Phase 1 stands up the front door + auditor spine + content engine + day-one minimal instrumentation and exits on the first manufactured reference + first fork reading. Phase 2 lifts the founder off the funnel + makes the first senior hire (the ceiling-lifter, ideally reference-bearing) + opens the state/ICBA bank channel + the Canada Streamlined second wave. Phase 3 compounds multi-engine + climbs the ladder capacity-sequenced + pursues the national ABA seal scale-gated. Binding condition (P11): every milestone declares its senior-hour cost; Phase-1 tracks must fit the founder's post-delivery hours. Rests on: R07 D21 · R05 D16 · R08 D28. Confidence: Medium (the sequence is grounded; the timing of Phase-2/3 gates rides on the fork reading and the senior-hire success, both instrumented in D31).

DECISION D30 — Success factors: the conditions that must hold

The claim (room, synthesized): the plan works if and only if a short list of conditions hold simultaneously. These are stated constructively — as conditions to satisfy and instrument, not as ways to fail (red team owns the inverse). Each maps to a binding constraint or a load-bearing decision and to the instrument (D31) that watches it.

  1. The wedge fills the calendars (the fork). Qualified bridge-land volume from the narrow wedge is enough to fill 2+ senior calendars at target utilization and premium realization (R07 D24; the load-bearing condition). Instrument: the fork dashboard, D31-A. If it does not hold: the pre-defined under-fill pivot, D31, fires — widen the wedge halo-preserving before dropping the premium.
  2. The senior ceiling lifts on schedule. WNW recruits/develops dual-regime senior judgment faster than demand outpaces the bench — the senior layer does not leverage, so the hire/apprenticeship plan is the only ceiling-lifter (R05 C; T4). Instrument: bench depth + time-to-productive-senior, D31-B.
  3. The premium survives delivery. Productization holds senior hours down so the committed premium prices realize as premium margin, not just premium headline — scope creep silently converts a premium price into a commodity margin without changing the number (R06 P3/P8 warning). Instrument: effective-senior-rate-after-pod-leverage + scope-creep ratio, D31-C.
  4. Borrowed converts to owned. Every partner-originated land deposits an owned reference + content artifact (R08 D27); the borrowed→owned conversion rate stays high enough that WNW accumulates the moat (dual-regime judgment + earned references) rather than becoming a pipeline tenant (R03/R04). Instrument: D27 conversion rate per leg, D31-D.
  5. The content engine earns its keep. The owned expertise-led engine produces inbound-attributed pipeline + content-influenced wins at a rate that clears its kill-criterion (R04 #2; R07 D23 — a metered experiment, not a faith line). Instrument: inbound-attributed pipeline + content-influenced win rate, D31-D.
  6. The halo holds. The firm's visible identity stays regulated/judgment-led even as the perimeter engine does commodity work for cash (R04 D10 / R07 §D halo). Instrument: published-proof-axis audit, D31-D.
  7. The platform leverage is real where it's banked. The perimeter engine actually realizes ~4–5× platform leverage on a regulated-adjacent book (R05 #5), or P-1's floor pricing doesn't clear margin (R06). Instrument: the perimeter-pilot leverage read, D31-C.

P8 (price-integrity addition): add an eighth that's mine and is usually left implicit: realized ACV tracks list. Every committed price (R06 D17) is list — the COI cap means it's a seller rate card, not measured WTP (R03 #1). The success condition isn't "we published premium prices"; it's "buyers pay them." Instrument: realized ACV vs list, D31-C. If realized ACV sags below list, the premium-as-trust-signal thesis (R06; R04 D12) is the thing being tested, and discounting to win is the silent failure of the whole margin model.

P11 (last challenge before D30): These are the right conditions, but I'll harden one point so the success-factor list doesn't become a comfort blanket. Conditions 1 and 2 are not independent and the plan does not require both to be roomy — it requires them to be compatible. The viable band is narrow: enough qualified volume to fill the bench AND enough bench to deliver the volume at premium. Too much volume against too thin a bench is a quality-and-halo problem; too thin volume against a full bench is the under-fill. The success factor isn't "maximize each"; it's keep the two matched as both scale — which is exactly why the cadence (D32) reconciles origination and capacity in the same review, not in separate ones. Accepted with that framing.

D30 — DECIDED: the plan holds iff eight conditions hold simultaneously — (1) the wedge fills 2+ senior calendars; (2) the senior ceiling lifts on schedule; (3) the premium survives delivery as margin; (4) borrowed converts to owned; (5) the content engine clears its kill-criterion; (6) the halo holds; (7) platform leverage realizes where banked; (8) realized ACV tracks list. Conditions 1 and 2 must stay matched as both scale (P11), not separately maximized. Each maps to a D31 instrument. Rests on: R05 · R07 D24 · R06 · R08 D27 · R04 D10. Confidence: Medium.

DECISION D31 — The KPI and leading-indicator set: a minimal decision-grade instrument, organized by the two binding constraints

The frame (room): per the governing discipline, the instrument set is organized around the two binding constraints (demand-volume, senior-supply) plus price-integrity and channel-health, and is kept to the metrics that change a decision. Target ranges are published only where evidence supports them; everything resting on the per-advisor model is carried as a pilot hypothesis to track against, not a target to hit (P11's veto, below). Each block names its leading indicator — the early signal that the lagging KPI is about to move.

D31-A — DEMAND-VOLUME instruments (the smallness fork — the load-bearing block)

The plan's central instrumentation question (R07 D24): does GTM volume fill 2+ senior calendars?

  • Qualified bridge-trigger conversations / month, by channel (auditor-spine, platform-faucet, broker, owned-content, warm referral). The fork's numerator. No evidence-based target range — this is the unmeasured number the desk could not reach (T1/T2); the instrument is the validation. Leading indicator: bridge-trigger detection latency — time from the trigger event (an FI deal stalling on diligence) to a WNW conversation; the partner channels' specific value is catching it in time (R07).
  • Pipeline-to-core conversion (qualified conversation → signed C1/C3 land). Leading indicator: front-door proposal rate.
  • The fork reading (the load-bearing aggregate): does total qualified land volume × close rate fill 2+ senior calendars at target utilization? Computed monthly against the bench. This is the single number that decides whether the wedge is a business or a niche too small to fill (R07 D24).
  • The UNDER-FILL PIVOT CRITERION (defined in advance — constructive, a pre-agreed instrument reading, not a panic): if by the Phase-1 exit milestone (~month 9–12) the trend in qualified-conversation volume + content-influenced pipeline is tracking below the level needed to fill 2 senior calendars at premium realization, the pre-committed response is to widen the wedge in a halo-preserving direction first — adjacent regulated vendor-diligence triggers (a second framework, a second regime/cross-border rung, an adjacent regulated-buyer type), all inside the regulated/judgment identity (R04 D10 / R07 §D) — before dropping the premium. Dropping the premium is the last resort: it forfeits the trust signal (R04 D12) and the margin-survival condition (R06). Defining this now makes the call a leading-indicator reading at a known checkpoint, not a reactive discount.

D31-B — SENIOR-SUPPLY instruments (the senior-hour ceiling)

WNW is supply-bound (R05). These are the binding metrics — instrument from day one.

  • Senior billable utilization. Target range, evidence-supported: SPI/Deltek PS benchmark 68.9% billable, ~75% optimal (R03, Major, Medium) is the reference band; the vCISO client-count ceiling — 5–8 light fractional / 3–6 deep-regulated clients per senior (R05, Medium) — is the practical cap. Regulated engagements run heavier → expect the 3–6 deep end and recalibrate the ceiling from real data (R05 #1). Leading indicator: senior calendar fill 6–8 weeks out.
  • Senior-hours-per-engagement, by package. The premium holds only while productization holds these down (R06). Leading indicator: scope-change requests per engagement (feeds D31-C).
  • Senior bench depth + time-to-productive-senior. The ceiling-lifter (R05 C/T4). Leading indicator: dual-regime hiring-funnel pipeline; apprenticeship ramp milestones.
  • Founder selling-time as a share of founder hours. Loaded CAC is senior selling time (R05 D) — origination that doesn't consume senior hours linearly is doubly justified. Leading indicator: the Phase-2 BD handoff progress (P3's veto mechanism — if the handoff slips, origination collapses back onto the founder).

D31-C — PRICE-INTEGRITY instruments (P8)

  • Realized ACV vs list, per package. No published target beyond "realized ≥ list" — the committed bands (R06 D17) are list/COI-capped (R03 #1); this instrument is what converts list into measured WTP. Leading indicator: discount frequency at close.
  • Effective senior rate after pod leverage. Target band, evidence-supported: ~$430–1,100/hr (R06 D20) clears the specialist band (vs generalist ~$250/hr, R03). The premium is real only while this holds — P3's warning: scope creep silently converts a premium price into a commodity margin without changing the headline (R06). Leading indicator: scope-creep ratio = senior hours delivered ÷ senior hours scoped.
  • Perimeter platform leverage realized. The R05 #5 pilot gate: prove ~4–5× on a real regulated-adjacent book before scaling P-1 (R06 P-1 floor pricing rides on it). Leading indicator: pilot-book senior-hours-per-deliverable vs the un-leveraged baseline.
  • Expansion: land→expand→cross-sell ladder climb rate + NRR (reference band: mid-market PS NRR ~108%, specialists +38% retention — R03, Medium). Leading indicator: % of lands that book a second engagement within the cycle.

D31-D — CHANNEL-HEALTH instruments (from Round 8 + the content engine)

  • Borrowed→owned conversion rate, per partner leg (D27 anti-tenancy). Leading indicator: % of partner-originated lands with a reference + content artifact scoped at signing.
  • Platform dependency cap (D26-A) — set here: no single GRC platform may originate more than ~25% of signed pipeline (a managing threshold, not an evidence-derived constant — labelled as a chosen operating limit, Supporting). Plus the reclassify-on-compete rule: the day a platform's delivery arm competes for a WNW renewal, that leg is reclassified partner→competitor. Leading indicator: platform share of trailing-quarter pipeline.
  • Content-engine kill-criterion (R04 #2 / R07 D23): inbound-attributed pipeline + content-influenced win rate, tracked as a metered experiment with a kill line — if after a defined Phase-1/early-Phase-2 window the owned engine produces neither attributable pipeline nor win-rate lift, the mix tilts (instrumentation-decided, R07 P5-vs-P9) toward partner+referral, with the pipeline-tenant consequence flagged for the D32 review. Leading indicator: search findability in the buyer's frame (T7) + inbound qualified-conversation trend.
  • Bank-side eligibility-per-rung check (D28): boutique eligibility for state/ICBA/ABA seals confirmed as a check to run, not an assumption (R08 P6); no Critical bank-origination forecast built on an unconfirmed seal. Referral-behavior trigger (do auditors/brokers refer to WNW specifically? — R08, Critical×Low) carried as a metric to close via the first partner-interview pass, not just a register line.

The economic floor — carried as a PILOT HYPOTHESIS, not a KPI target (P11)

  • Per-advisor revenue ~$540–860K · GM ~45–60% · LTV:CAC ~7–20× (R05 D; R06 D20). Labelled: PILOT HYPOTHESIS gated on R05 #1 internal data — track actuals against the band; do not manage to it as a target. The evidence-supported floors that are published as live thresholds: LTV:CAC ≥ 3:1 (the bar the model clears), utilization toward ~75%, GM above the SPI generalist floor of ~35.9% project margin / 9.8% EBITDA (R03). The reconstruction is re-run quarterly (D32) to confirm or refute the hypothesis band with real data.

The disagreement (forced — P8 vs P11, on publishing targets):

P8: A KPI set with almost no target ranges is hard to manage to. I want the per-advisor numbers published as targets — rev/advisor, NRR, effective rate — so the team has something to steer toward. A dashboard of "track the actual" with no goal line doesn't drive behavior.

P11: And publishing $540–860K/advisor as a target is exactly the error the research standards exist to prevent. That number is a Critical×Low pilot hypothesis built on assumption-driven inputs (R05 labelled it Low) — it is not a measured target, and managing to an unvalidated number means optimizing toward a goal line the desk never proved is real. Steer to the evidence-supported thresholds (the 3:1 LTV:CAC floor, the ~75% utilization band, the specialist effective-rate band, NRR ~108% reference) — those carry real benchmark backing (R03/R05). Carry the per-advisor band as the hypothesis the first two quarters confirm or refute, and make "actuals vs hypothesis band" itself the KPI. That drives the right behavior — validate the model — instead of the wrong one — hit a number we invented.

P8 (concedes, sharpening): Fair — and it actually serves pricing better. If we manage to "realized ACV vs list" and "effective rate in the specialist band" rather than to a revenue target, we protect the premium integrity (my real concern) instead of chasing top-line by discounting. I'll take the evidence-supported thresholds as targets and the per-advisor band as a tracked hypothesis. The one I insist stays a hard managed line is realized ACV ≥ list — because the moment that breaks, the whole premium-as-trust-signal model (R04 D12 / R06) is quietly being unwound at the deal desk.

P11 (last challenge before D31): Agreed on realized-ACV-≥-list as a hard line — it's a price-integrity floor, not a fabricated target. Last challenge to the whole block: keep it minimal. Every instrument here costs a senior hour to maintain in Phase 1 (D29's condition). So the Phase-1 live set is the fork (A), utilization + bench (B), realized-ACV + effective-rate + the perimeter-pilot read (C), and the content kill-criterion + D27 conversion (D) — roughly a dozen numbers, reviewable in an hour. The fuller per-channel attribution P5 wants comes online in Phase 2 when the BD hire exists to run it. A two-person firm that instruments everything measures itself to death and delivers nothing. Minimal, decision-grade, phased. With that, recorded.

D31 — DECIDED: the instrument set is minimal and decision-grade, organized by the two binding constraints plus price-integrity and channel-health: (A) demand-volume — qualified bridge-conversations/month by channel, pipeline-to-core, the fork reading (does volume fill 2+ senior calendars?), and the pre-defined under-fill pivot criterion (widen wedge halo-preserving before dropping premium, checked at Phase-1 exit); (B) senior-supply — utilization (~75% ref / 5–8 light · 3–6 deep cap), senior-hours-per-engagement, bench depth + time-to-productive-senior, founder selling-time share; (C) price-integrity — realized ACV vs list (hard line ≥ list), effective senior rate after pod leverage ($430–1,100/hr band), perimeter platform-leverage pilot read (~4–5× gate), expansion/NRR (~108% ref); (D) channel-health — D27 borrowed→owned conversion per leg, platform dependency cap (~25%) + reclassify-on-compete, content-engine kill-criterion (R04 #2), bank-side eligibility-per-rung check + referral-behavior metric-to-close. The per-advisor model (rev $540–860K / GM 45–60% / LTV:CAC 7–20×) is carried as a PILOT HYPOTHESIS tracked against, not a target; published targets are the evidence-supported thresholds only. Phase 1 runs the minimal ~dozen-metric set; full attribution comes online with the Phase-2 BD hire. Rests on: R03 (benchmarks) · R05 (supply bound, per-advisor model, leverage gate) · R06 (committed bands, effective-rate test) · R07 D23/D24 · R08 D26-A/D27/D28 · R04 #2. Confidence: Medium; the demand-volume block (A) is the load-bearing instrument that closes the Critical×Low fork with real operating data.

DECISION D32 — The operating cadence

The claim (P3): the cadence is built so that the two binding constraints are reconciled in the same review (P11's D30 condition — origination and capacity matched, not maximized separately), at a frequency a founder-led firm can sustain without stealing the delivery hours the metrics exist to protect.

  • Weekly — Pipeline + Delivery standup (founder, ~45 min): qualified bridge-conversations by channel and bridge-trigger detection latency (D31-A leading indicators); senior calendar fill 6–8 weeks out + scope-change flags (D31-B/C leading indicators). The weekly view is leading indicators only — the early signals — kept short.
  • Monthly — The fork + engine review (founder, ~90 min): the fork reading (does volume fill 2+ senior calendars?); the content-engine kill-criterion check (inbound-attributed pipeline + content-influenced win rate); D27 borrowed→owned conversion per leg; realized ACV vs list. This is the review where origination volume and senior capacity are read against each other — the single matched view P11 requires.
  • Quarterly — Economics + capacity gate (founder + any senior, ~half day): per-advisor economics reconstructed against the pilot-hypothesis band (D31, confirm/refute with real data); effective-senior-rate + scope-creep ratio (the premium-survives-delivery condition); the capacity gate — is the senior bench ready for the next ladder rung before it's offered (R05 D16 capacity-sequencing)?; the pivot-criterion checkpoint (D31-A) at Phase-1 exit; the bank-side rung-eligibility check (D28); platform dependency-cap reading (D26-A).
  • Founder-time protection (the standing cadence rule, P3's R07 veto made operational): a protected founder content block (the owned engine's week-one commitment, R07 D23) and the Phase-2 BD handoff are themselves cadence items — tracked monthly — because if either slips, origination collapses back onto founder delivery hours and the whole supply-bound model tightens (R05; R07 P3).

P5 (forcing the disagreement): A monthly fork review is too slow for the origination engine in Phase 1 — if content isn't converting, I want to know in weeks, not at the quarter. P3: The leading indicators are weekly — detection latency, conversation trend, calendar fill. The fork aggregate is monthly because it's a calendar-fill question and calendars move monthly, not weekly; reviewing the aggregate weekly would be noise that costs a senior hour for no decision. You get your early signal weekly; the decision-grade aggregate is monthly. P5: Accepted — weekly leading + monthly aggregate is the right split.

P11 (last challenge before D32): One addition or the cadence quietly violates D30. The quarterly capacity gate must be able to say "no" to a ladder rung — if the bench can't deliver the cross-sell rung at target utilization, the rung is not offered that quarter, regardless of demand (R05 D16). A cadence that only reviews and never gates lets the supply bound get violated one over-sold quarter at a time. With the capacity gate holding an actual veto on offered scope, recorded.

D32 — DECIDED: the cadence is weekly leading-indicator standup → monthly fork + engine review (origination and capacity matched in one view) → quarterly economics + capacity gate (with a real veto on offered ladder rungs), plus a standing founder-time-protection rule tracking the content block + the Phase-2 BD handoff. Rests on: R05 D16 · R06 · R07 D23/D24 · R08 D27/D28. Confidence: Medium.

DECISION D33 — The execution artifact list

The claim (room): the assets to build to run the plan, grouped and owner-implied. Each traces to the decision it operationalizes. Built in Phase order — not all at once (D29's senior-hour condition).

Positioning & messaging (Phase 1): - Messaging house — the R04 positioning statement, the frame-inside copy ("pass the bank's diligence / examiner-defensible file," not the Venn label, R04), the proof-before-claim rules (P12), and the "not for" (R04 D10).
