Gated by T7 frame-recognition + the WNW credibility inventory (publishing precondition, R04). - Sales playbook — the Bridge-Engagement discovery script, the two-motion scripts (SaaS-fast / bank-slow, R01 D3), objection handling, the dual-artifact close.

Pricing & packaging (Phase 1): - Pricing sheet — the committed bands (R06 D17), the two value-metric calculators (SaaS = % of blocked ARR; bank = avoided AMP/MRA + CISO-replacement, R06 D18), the fixed-fee front-door spec. - Productized Bridge-Engagement spec — fixed scope/time/fee, the dual-artifact templates (SaaS deal-unblock package + the examiner-legible artifact per SR 24-2 that doubles as the bank same-industry reference, R05 D14).

Delivery & capacity (Phase 1): - Delivery pod playbook — RACI by engine (senior judgment / junior commodity / platform automatable, R05 D16); the capacity-gate line-item declaration (engine + senior-hour cost per line). - Perimeter "readiness factory" SOP + platform-leverage pilot protocol — the R05 #5 pilot design that proves ~4–5× before P-1 scales. - Senior-hire / apprenticeship plan + dual-regime talent spec (Phase 1 drafted, Phase 2 executed) — the ceiling-lifter; reference-bearing pedigree prioritized (R04→R09 hiring note; R02 bank-first fork).

Partner (Phase 1–2): - Partner one-pagers, per leg — auditor reciprocal-handoff, GRC-platform co-sell, broker readiness-review, association member-benefit, fractional (R08 D26). - Anti-tenancy conversion checklist — reference + content artifact as scoped deliverables with up-front consent, published on the regulated axis (R08 D27).

Content & origination (Phase 1, compounding): - Content-engine editorial system — wedge-scoped, buyer's-frame, sustainable founder cadence, instrumented with the kill-criterion (R07 D23 / R04 #2). - Reference / case-study library — segmented; regulated/judgment axis only to protect the halo (R04 / R07 §D).

Measurement (Phase 1): - The instrumentation dashboard — the D31 minimal set (the fork + two-constraint KPIs + leading indicators). - The validation-trigger register — the buyer-probe + internal-data pulls (the single buyer engagement + single internal pull that closes the consolidated T1/T2/T5/T7 + R03#1 + R04#1 + R05#1 + referral-behavior family), with owners and timing; the day-one instruments (D31) are what close most of it from real operating data.

P11 (last challenge before D33): The list is right; the discipline is sequence, which I'll bind. If all of these are "Phase 1," none of them is — the founder can't build a messaging house, a pricing sheet, five partner one-pagers, a content system, and a dashboard while delivering the engagements that generate the references the content system needs (R05; D29). So: the irreducible Phase-1 set is the productized Bridge-Engagement spec + pricing sheet + the auditor one-pager + the content editorial system + the minimal dashboard — the five assets without which the first land can't be sold, delivered, instrumented, or converted. The rest (full messaging house polish, the other four partner one-pagers, the reference library at scale) build as the engagements that populate them arrive. An artifact with no engagement to fill it is a senior hour spent on a template instead of a client. Recorded.

D33 — DECIDED: the artifact list is grouped (messaging · pricing/packaging · delivery/capacity · partner · content/origination · measurement), owner-implied, and built in phase order — the irreducible Phase-1 five are the Bridge-Engagement spec, the pricing sheet, the auditor one-pager, the content editorial system, and the minimal dashboard; the rest build as the engagements that populate them arrive (P11). Rests on: R04 · R05 D14/D16 · R06 D17/D18 · R07 D23 · R08 D26/D27. Confidence: Medium.

The instrument is the validation; no desk source can close it.

  • Platform/association program economics [Supporting×Low; R08] — the dependency cap (D26-A, threshold set at ~25% in D31-D) and the eligibility-per-rung check (D28) are the operating hedges until program conversations close it.

Re-bound: the R07 D21 owned-vs-borrowed mix → instrumentation-decided via the content kill-criterion + D27 conversion rate (D31-D), exactly as Round 8 deferred to here; R02#3 platform-encroachment-speed → the dependency-cap reading + reclassify-on-compete (D31-D); R05's senior-hour ceiling → the binding D31-B block.

Round 9 decisions, in one place

  • D29 — Execution roadmap: three phased milestone tracks on the R07-D21 motion (Origination · Delivery/Capacity · Partner · Measurement), dated from month 0 = Jul 2026, owners implied. Phase 3 (24+): multi-engine compounding + ladder climbed capacity-sequenced + national ABA scale-gated. Binding: every milestone declares its senior-hour cost.
  • D30 — Success factors: eight conditions that must hold simultaneously (wedge fills 2+ calendars · senior ceiling lifts on schedule · premium survives delivery as margin · borrowed converts to owned · content engine clears its kill-criterion · halo holds · platform leverage realizes · realized ACV tracks list); conditions 1 and 2 kept matched as both scale, not separately maximized.
  • D31 — KPI + leading-indicator set: minimal, decision-grade, organized by the two binding constraints + price-integrity + channel-health. Demand-volume block (A) is the load-bearing fork instrument, with the under-fill pivot criterion defined in advance (widen wedge halo-preserving before dropping premium). Per-advisor model carried as a tracked pilot hypothesis, not a target; published targets are the evidence-supported thresholds only (LTV:CAC ≥ 3:1, util ~75%, effective rate $430–1,100/hr, NRR ~108%); realized-ACV-≥-list is the one hard price line. Phase-1 runs ~a dozen metrics; full attribution arrives with the Phase-2 BD hire.
  • D32 — Operating cadence: weekly leading-indicator standup → monthly fork + engine review (origination and capacity matched in one view) → quarterly economics + capacity gate (with a real veto on offered ladder rungs); standing founder-time-protection rule tracking the content block + the Phase-2 BD handoff.
  • D33 — Execution artifact list: grouped (messaging · pricing/packaging · delivery/capacity · partner · content · measurement), owner-implied, built in phase order — the irreducible Phase-1 five are the Bridge-Engagement spec, the pricing sheet, the auditor one-pager, the content editorial system, and the minimal dashboard; the rest build as the engagements that populate them arrive.

Round 10 — Integration Stress

Phase: INTEGRATION (last deliberation round before Synthesis) Date: 2026-06-27 Moderator: convening per MODERATOR.md Round 10. Roster (conflict-bearing + Skeptic): P12 Strategic Skeptic (LEADS); P5 GTM & Demand Lead; P9 Partnerships & Ecosystem Builder; P1 SaaS Buyer; P2 Regulated Buyer; P3 Boutique Operator; P11 Unit-Economics & Capacity Modeler; P7 Regulatory & Frameworks Authority; P8 Pricing & Packaging Architect; P6 Competitive & Market Analyst; P10 Trust & Buyer-Psychology Expert. Nature of the round: internal-consistency and strongest-version pass. NOT failure-point red-teaming (MODERATOR.md Round 10 + Rule 10 — the red team owns failure points AFTER synthesis). No new risks are authored here; contradictions are reconciled and open assumptions are recorded as validation triggers.

0. Gate-check (top of round, per MODERATOR.md + STATE.md next_unit)

Question: does reconciling any Critical contradiction in this round require grounding that desk web research can reach but we have not yet commissioned (R06 regulatory-primaries / R09 cyber-insurance / R10 ai-governance-demand)?

Moderator ruling: NO commission. Integration reconciles decisions D1–D33 that are already accepted on accepted research R01–R05 + R07 + R08 (+ brief). It introduces no new market claim that needs fresh sourcing — it tests whether the accepted pieces cohere. The three pending files feed durability/insurer-demand/AI-forecast colour, none of which is the hinge of an unreconciled Critical contradiction:

  • R06 (regulatory-primaries) would raise the regulatory-interpretation durability sub-leg (R03 H3) from Medium toward High. But D12's moat rests on four independent barriers, with the scarce dual-regime senior-talent wall (R05, accepted) as the primary; the regulatory-edge leg is the durability sub-leg only, correctly held at Medium and flagged (R04 gate-check §126). No integration contradiction turns on lifting it.
  • R09 (cyber-insurance) would corroborate leg C's demand basis. But R08 already established leg C's mechanism (broker "optimizes for renewal not pass" = the gap-fill opening), which is what the Tier-2 exchange decision (D26-C) needed. The insurer leg is Tier-2, not load-bearing for coherence.
  • R10 (ai-governance-demand) feeds an item the brief itself flags as Forecast/Low and which D5 explicitly held out of the demand pillars (instrumented, not built on). Nothing in the reconciliation rests on it.

The one genuinely unliftable input — buyer WTP + qualified demand-volume for this exact niche (the smallness fork) — is not desk-reachable at all. It is already the signed, load-bearing Critical×Low validation trigger (T1/T2, R07 D24). No pending file would touch it. The Skeptic concurs (recorded below). Gate resolved: proceed to integration on the accepted stack.

1. The Skeptic frames the round (P12 leads)

P12 (Strategic Skeptic): "My job here is not to break the plan — the red team does that next. My job is to confirm the plan is the strongest version of itself and internally coherent, and to make sure every place where we are still guessing is written down as a trigger, not smuggled in as a fact. I am going to run three coherence questions the Moderator handed me, then force-close the six dissents that have been threading the rounds, then consolidate the trigger register the synthesis will carry. I will steelman a contradiction at each step; if the room closes too fast I reopen it.

Before any of that, I want the room to agree on the shape of this plan in one sentence, because coherence is judged against that shape: WNW is a supply-bound boutique that dominates one narrow bridge — the regulated software-to-bank vendor-diligence trust chain — by manufacturing examiner-legible references off a productized front door, priced on a specialization premium, originated mainly through partners who can see the bridge trigger, and gated throughout on whether that one narrow wedge produces enough qualified volume to fill two-plus senior calendars at premium prices. Every coherence test below asks: does each component fit that shape, or does it quietly assume a different business? Let's go."

The room accepts the framing. The Moderator notes it matches the accepted decision stack (R01 D1–D4 bridge/two-motion; R02 D5/D6 demand-quality=wedge + bridge-domination sequence; R03 D7/D8 holdable band; R04 D9–D12 positioning; R05 D13–D16 two-engine catalog; R06 D17–D20 pricing; R07 D21–D24 motion; R08 D25–D28 partnerships; R09 D29–D33 execution).

2. Coherence Question (a) — Does the PRICING (R06 D17–D20) fit the ICP (R01 D1–D4)?

P12 (steelman of the contradiction): "Here is the strongest version of 'these don't fit.' R01 gave us two ICPs with two value metrics and two motions — SaaS (fast, deal-unblock, individual-led) and Bank (slow, examiner-defensibility, documented). R06 then committed one premium pricing philosophy ('price the engine not the service; price is a trust signal; never hourly'). If the SaaS buyer (P1) is, by definition, the one who refuses consulting theater and open-ended retainers and wants the cheapest fastest outcome — then a premium price philosophy is a category error for half the ICP. You priced for the bank and bolted the SaaS buyer on. That's the incoherence. Defend it."

P8 (Pricing Architect): "It survives, and here's the mechanism — the premium is not attached to the buyer's segment, it is attached to the engine, and the engine split (R05 D13/D16) cuts across both ICPs, not along the segment line. The dividing line is whether the work consumes a senior judgment-hour. So: - The CORE engine (C1 Bridge, C2 SaaS retainer, C3 bank TPRM/exam-prep, C4 bank retainer, C5 cross-sell) is priced on the specialization premium — for both segments — because in both segments the thing being bought is scarce dual-regime judgment, and R03 C established specialization commands a documented premium (generalist ~$250/hr vs specialist $600+/hr). - The PERIMETER engine (P-1 readiness factory) is priced at/near the platform floor (~$8–18K) — for the SaaS volume buyer who genuinely is price-sensitive and genuinely is buying a commodity.

So P1's price-sensitivity is honoured — on the perimeter, where it belongs. P1's premium resistance never touches the core, because the core SaaS product (C1 Bridge) is sold to a different P1 in a different state: not the generic SaaS buyer shopping SOC-2, but the bridge buyer whose FI deal just stalled (R04 D11). For that buyer, R04 D10's reconciliation holds — regulated depth is the deal-unblock, so premium is the fast outcome they want. The price fits the ICP because the wedge ICP is not the generic SaaS ICP."

P1 (SaaS Buyer): "I'll concede the structure, with one hard condition I already won in R05/R06 and want re-confirmed here: the core SaaS price (C1 $30–45K fixed) only reads as 'fast outcome' and not 'consulting theater' if it stays productized, fixed-fee, and finish-lined. The moment it becomes an open-ended retainer sold cold, you've lost me — and the reconciliation in D17/D19 (hybrid retainer entered off a delivered land, never sold cold) is what keeps it coherent. If anyone in execution lets the front door drift into an open retainer pitch, the price stops fitting my ICP and P12's contradiction comes true. So my concession is conditional on the D19 sequencing holding in the field — which is exactly what R09 D31's realized-ACV-≥-list and scope-creep instrument watches."

P2 (Regulated Buyer): "From my side the fit is cleaner and I'll say so plainly: the bank ICP wants a price that signals seriousness. A cheap examiner-defensibility engagement reads as a red flag to a risk officer — 'if it were this cheap, it wouldn't survive the exam.' R06's 'price is a trust signal' (cost tips only ~8%, R07 §A) fits my ICP exactly. The only place I push: C3/C4's premium must be justifiable to an examiner as well as to me — R06 already bound P2's examiner-justifiability test (FDIC) as the ceiling. Held."

P11 (Capacity Modeler): "The fit I care about is arithmetic, and R06 already proved it: the committed prices reproduce the R05 per-advisor model (5–6 retainers @ $9–14K/mo blend = $540–860K rev/advisor, 45–60% GM) rather than inventing a new one. That's the strongest possible coherence proof — pricing and capacity are the same model expressed twice. But I re-flag my R06 finding because it is the hinge of question (b) too: premium pricing controls only one of the two knife-edge variables. It is necessary, not sufficient. The second variable is utilization, which is volume-dependent. So pricing 'fits the ICP' as a model — but whether the model runs depends on the wedge supplying the volume to fill the books. Pricing↔ICP coheres; pricing↔capacity is gated on the fork. Don't let the clean answer here paper over that."

P12 (last challenge on (a)): "Accept it, with P11's flag carried forward verbatim. One residual I won't let pass silently: the whole fit rests on the wedge ICP being the bridge buyer, not the generic SaaS buyer. If T1/T7 come back saying the bridge buyer doesn't self-identify into the frame — if they shop this as generic SOC-2 — then the premium does become a category error and P1's resistance returns at full strength. So (a) coheres conditional on T7 (frame recognition) + T1 (intersection demand). Logged, not smoothed."

> DECISION D34(a): PRICING ↔ ICP — COHERENT, conditionally. The premium philosophy attaches to the engine (senior-judgment-hour = core = premium; commodity = perimeter = floor), which cuts across both ICPs rather than along the segment line, so P1's price-sensitivity is honoured on the perimeter and P1's premium-resistance never touches the core because the core wedge ICP is the bridge buyer, not the generic SaaS buyer (R04 D10/D11). Pricing reproduces the R05 capacity model (P11), so pricing↔ICP is the same model expressed twice. Conditions carried: (i) P1's front door stays productized/fixed/finish-lined; hybrid retainer entered only off a delivered land (D17/D19), instrumented by realized-ACV-≥-list + scope-creep (R09 D31); (ii) coherence rides on the wedge ICP being the bridge buyer — gated T7 + T1. P11's flag: pricing↔ICP coheres as a model; whether the model runs is the volume question reserved to (b).

3. Coherence Question (b) — Does the CHANNEL (R07 D21–D24 / R08 D25–D28) fit the CAPACITY (R05 supply-bound + R09 scaffolding)?

P12 (steelman of the contradiction): "Strongest version: you have built a channel machine — owned content engine (P5), five partner currencies (P9), two non-shared segment channels, a manufactured-referability flywheel — to pour qualified conversations into a firm that, by its own decisive finding (R05), cannot deliver them, because it is supply-bound on senior judgment-hours, not demand-bound. You have spent nine rounds optimizing the wrong constraint. A supply-bound firm that builds a world-class demand engine just generates a longer waitlist and burns founder-selling-hours (which R05 says are the loaded CAC, stolen from delivery) creating demand it must then turn away. That is an incoherent plan: channel sized for a demand-bound business, capacity sized for a supply-bound one. Reconcile it."

P5 (GTM Lead): "This is the sharpest challenge in the round and the answer is the frame R07 was built on, so it's already load-bearing: budget origination in senior-hours consumed, not dollars or leads. The channel plan is not 'maximize demand.' It is 'originate the most qualified volume per senior-hour spent,' precisely because senior hours are the binding constraint. That's why the engines are ranked by senior-hour cost: (1) borrowed pipeline ≈0 senior-hrs/lead, (2) owned content front-loaded-to-create then ≈0 marginal, (3) cold outbound cut as an engine. A supply-bound firm doesn't build no channel — it builds the channel that doesn't consume the scarce resource to run. The flywheel is chosen over outbound because outbound spends senior selling-hours linearly and the flywheel doesn't. So the channel is shaped by the capacity constraint, not in ignorance of it. P12's 'longer waitlist' only happens if we over-originate; the fix is in the cadence."

P3 (Operator): "And the cadence is the fix — R09 D32 makes origination and capacity reconcile in the same monthly review, not in separate ones, and the quarterly capacity gate holds a real veto on offered ladder rungs. That is the structural answer to 'longer waitlist': we don't offer a rung the current senior bench can't deliver at target utilization (R05 D16 capacity-sequencing). The channel can't outrun capacity because the gate won't let it. P12's incoherence assumes demand-gen and delivery are run by different people optimizing different numbers — R09 deliberately fused them into one review precisely so that can't happen. My own veto (founder-time protection) is the same mechanism: if origination starts eating delivery hours, the cadence catches it monthly."

P9 (Partnerships): "There's a second reason the channel fits the capacity, and it's the strongest one: the highest-quality leg is also the lowest-senior-hour leg. The auditor/CPA spine (D26-B) is regulation-forced (AICPA independence bars the attestor from doing the prep), so it costs ≈0 senior-hours to cultivate and delivers the warmest, most durable lead and is the bridge-trigger detector (R07 — 3 of 4 parties who see a stalled-diligence event are partners). For a supply-bound firm that is the ideal channel: it doesn't spend the scarce resource to run, and it catches the one high-intent event in time. The platform faucet (D26-A) is the opposite coordinate — high volume, low trust — and is deliberately quarantined and dependency-capped (~25%, R09 D31-D) exactly so it can't flood a supply-bound delivery org. The channel portfolio is self-rationing toward the legs a capacity-constrained firm can actually serve."

P11 (Capacity Modeler): "I'll grant the channel is shaped by the constraint. But I want the contradiction's true residue named, because P5/P9/P3 have answered the wrong half. The channel fitting capacity is settled. The unsettled thing is the one I flagged in (a): does the channel produce enough volume from a wedge this narrow to fill the books — not too much (the waitlist problem, solved by the gate), but too little (the under-fill problem, not solved by anything in the room)? R05 says we don't break on demand/CAC/LTV (~7–20×); we break only if total qualified volume from the narrow wedge is too thin to fill 2+ senior calendars. The channel is architected to maximize volume from a narrow wedge (R07 D24) — multi-engine, highest-intent event, capacity-cheap — and that's the best desk-reachable answer. But it is not proof the volume exists. So channel↔capacity coheres on the too-much side (gate + cadence) and is gated on the too-little side (the fork)."

P1 / P2 (the channel-pace sub-tension, surfaced here because it's a capacity question too): P1: "One coherence snag I want resolved, not waved: R02 D6 sequences SaaS-fast channel first (access) earning the regulated identity second (quality). But R04 anchored the visible identity on the regulated side from day one. My live warning (carried from R07): if the regulated anchor makes the SaaS-fast access channel slow and heavy — if every front-door conversation has to lead with 'examiner-defensible dual-regime' — it breaks its own access channel. The fast channel can't be fast if it's wearing the slow channel's clothes." P2: "And my counter, also carried: if the front door isn't positioned as regulated vendor-diligence, the bridge never earns the bank side (R02 D6 condition + halo F8). So the anchor must be visible." P12 (forcing it): "This is a real contradiction and it's a capacity one — selling effort is senior-hours. Resolve it or carry it."

P10 (Trust expert, adjudicating the pace tension): "It resolves on which buyer is in which frame, same move as R04. The regulated anchor is heavy for the generic SaaS buyer (who's in a 'check the SOC-2 box' frame) but it is the fast, native vocabulary for the bridge buyer (who's in a 'my FI deal just stalled on security diligence' frame). To the bridge buyer, 'examiner-defensible dual-regime vendor diligence' isn't slow consulting-speak — it's the exact words for their emergency. So the anchor doesn't slow the access channel when the access channel is scoped to the bridge buyer (R04 D11 wedge). It would slow a generic-SaaS access channel — which is precisely why D10 excludes generic SaaS from the visible identity. P1's warning is real and stays an instrument (R07 D24(c): does the regulated anchor suppress SaaS-fast origination speed?), but it is not an unreconciled contradiction — it's a frame-match question already answered in principle and already gated on T7."

P12 (last challenge on (b)): "Accepted, and I'll sharpen the residue so synthesis can't lose it. Channel↔capacity is coherent on every axis the room controls: (i) the channel is senior-hour-budgeted, so it's shaped by the constraint not against it (P5); (ii) the cadence + capacity-gate-with-veto prevent over-origination/waitlist (P3); (iii) the portfolio self-rations toward low-senior-hour high-trust legs (P9); (iv) the pace tension resolves on frame-match (P10), instrumented on T7. The one thing it cannot settle on desk evidence is whether the narrow wedge yields enough volume — the under-fill side. That is the fork. It is not a coherence defect; it is the plan's single load-bearing unknown, and it is already a signed trigger with a pre-defined response (R09 D31 under-fill pivot: widen wedge halo-preserving before dropping premium). Coherent, gated, instrumented. Move."

> DECISION D34(b): CHANNEL ↔ CAPACITY — COHERENT, with the under-fill fork as the single gated unknown. The channel is shaped by the supply-bound constraint, not against it: origination is budgeted in senior-hours consumed (R07 frame), engines ranked by that cost (borrowed ≈0 → owned front-loaded → cold cut); the portfolio self-rations toward the auditor spine (high-trust, ≈0 senior-hrs, bridge-detector) and quarantines/caps the platform faucet (R08 D26-A + R09 D31-D ~25%); the monthly fused review + quarterly capacity-gate-with-veto (R09 D32) structurally prevent the channel outrunning delivery (the over-origination/waitlist failure mode is closed). The P1↔P2 channel-pace tension resolves on frame-match (P10): the regulated anchor is fast vocabulary for the bridge buyer and slow only for the generic SaaS buyer whom D10 already excludes — instrumented as R07 D24(c), gated T7. The one unsettled axis: whether the narrow wedge yields enough volume to fill 2+ senior calendars (the under-fill side) — not a coherence defect but the plan's primary load-bearing trigger (T1/T2), already signed with a pre-defined under-fill pivot (R09 D31).

4. Coherence Question (c) — Does the POSITIONING (R04 D9–D12) survive the COMPETITIVE MAP (R02/R03 D7–D8)?

P12 (steelman of the contradiction): "Strongest version, and I'm giving P6 the ammunition: R04 positioned WNW as 'the dual-regime vendor-diligence & examiner-defensibility specialist for the regulated software-to-bank trust chain.' R02/R03 mapped the competitive ground and found the borders are moving — the automation line is rising (Cynomi climbed into the retainer band on a $37M Series B AI vCISO raise; Vanta/Drata service-partner programs are both channel and up-market threat), and the Big-4 productize downward. So the positioning describes a band that R03 itself called a slowly-closing gap, not a static one (P6 'the borders move'). You can't anchor a durable position on a melting iceberg. The position survives the competitive map today and is obsoleted by it tomorrow. Defend the durability, not just the existence."

P6 (Competitive Analyst): "I authored 'the borders move,' so let me say precisely what it does and doesn't threaten — because R03 D8 already drew this line and the positioning was built to sit on the durable side of it. The competitive map has layers, and encroachment hits them differently: - Commodity/automatable layer (evidence collection, control mapping, first-pass readiness, baseline vCISO reporting): compressing toward platform price, not holdable. The positioning explicitly does not stand here — D10 excludes commodity SOC-2 from the visible identity; it's the perimeter engine, priced at the floor, never positioned. So Cynomi climbing the retainer band attacks a band WNW deliberately doesn't claim as identity. - Channel layer (GRC partner programs): a double edge — usable, not ownable. The positioning doesn't claim to own it; R08 D26-A uses it as a capped faucet and reclassifies-on-compete. Consistent. - Judgment/interpretation + cross-regime + earned-trust band: R03 D8 found this is the narrower holdable space — held by a three-barrier wall (above the automation line / below the Big-4 floor / requires scarce dual-regime senior judgment). This is where D9–D12 positions. The question is only: does this band move?

My honest answer: the automation line is rising under it, but it rises into the commodity layer, not the judgment layer — Cynomi automates evidence and reporting, not 'defend this principles-based interpretation to a skeptical examiner across two regimes.' R03 H1 (judgment holdable, commodity not) and H3 (durable edge = principles-interpretation, not the perishable control crosswalk) are exactly the durability hedges. The positioning survives the map because it was drawn to occupy the layer the map shows isn't compressing."

P7 (Regulatory Authority): "I'll reinforce and bound the durability leg, because it's mine and I capped it myself. The moat's longevity sub-leg is principles-interpretation, not the FFIEC↔OSFI control crosswalk (R03 H3) — you can template a crosswalk (and Big-4 will), but you can't template defending a principle to an examiner. That's durable. My cap stands: I held this at Medium pending R06, and R06 is still pending. So the positioning survives the competitive map on the primary barrier (scarce dual-regime talent, R05/accepted/High) and the cross-border-is-real fact (brief S33/S34, Primary/High) — and the regulatory-interpretation durability sub-leg adds longevity at Medium, flagged. That's the correct cell for a Critical×Medium leg that isn't solely load-bearing. The positioning doesn't depend on my leg being High; it's one of four barriers."

P10 (Trust expert): "And the barrier the competitive map can't show on an axis chart is the one I own: earned trust doesn't commoditize on the same curve as tooling. A platform can automate the deliverable; it cannot automate the peer referral (71% find firms by asking a person, R07/Hinge) or the same-industry reference (+37% credibility) or the operator pedigree. R03 D8's third barrier and R04 D12's proof hierarchy sit outside the automation curve entirely. So even as the tooling borders move, the trust border holds on a different clock. That's why the positioning survives a moving map: three of its four barriers (talent, cross-border-fact, earned-trust) don't move on the automation line at all, and the fourth (regulatory-interpretation durability) moves slowly and is flagged."

P12 (last challenge on (c)): "Good — this is the cleanest of the three, because R03 D8 did the work in advance: the position was defined as the holdable sub-band, not the empty cell. I'll record the one durability condition with teeth: the map does move, so the positioning survives conditional on the encroachment-speed instrument (R02#3) — a measured rate of platform compression into the $8–22K/mo band — staying slower than the firm's ability to climb. And on my standing fork: 'empty and holdable' on the judgment/trust layers (gated T1/T5 demand, T4 talent, T2 sizing); 'empty for a reason' only on the commodity layer (compressed) and as a standalone both-sides play (no barrier — which is why the positioning is dual-regime bridge, not 'we serve software and banks'). The positioning survives the competitive map. The double-edged smallness — same narrowness that walls out Big-4 could make the firm sub-scale — is the sizing question behind the whole wedge and routes to the fork, not to a positioning defect."

> DECISION D34(c): POSITIONING ↔ COMPETITIVE MAP — SURVIVES. R03 D8 pre-drew the line: the position was defined as the holdable sub-band (judgment/interpretation + cross-regime + earned-trust), not the empty Venn cell. The moving borders (rising automation line; Big-4 productizing downward; GRC double-edge) attack the commodity layer, which D10 excludes from the visible identity and prices at the floor (perimeter engine) — so encroachment hits a band WNW deliberately doesn't claim. Three of the four moat barriers (scarce dual-regime talent [R05/High], cross-border-is-real [brief Primary/High], earned-trust [R07/off-the-automation-curve]) don't move on the automation line; the fourth (regulatory-interpretation durability, R03 H3 / P7) moves slowly and is held Medium, flagged, pending R06 — correct for a leg that is one of four, not solely load-bearing. Condition carried: durability is gated on encroachment-speed (R02#3) staying slower than WNW's ability to climb. The double-edged smallness routes to the fork (sizing), not to a positioning defect.

The room did not have to change a decision to make the set cohere — it had to name the conditions under which the already-made decisions hold together. That is the strongest possible integration outcome: the plan is internally consistent, and its open edges are all external (buyer/partner/internal data we can't reach from the desk), not internal (decisions that fight each other).

> DECISION D34: COHERENCE PASS — the choice set is internally consistent. Pricing fits the ICP (engine-not-segment premium); channel fits capacity (senior-hour-budgeted + gated cadence); positioning survives the competitive map (occupies the pre-drawn holdable sub-band). No decision was reversed. All carried conditions are external validation triggers, consolidated in §7.

6. Reconciling the six carried live dissents (P12 leads each; strongest-version, then resolution)

The Skeptic walks the six dissents that have threaded R01–R09 (STATE.md carry-forward). Each is either reconciled by structure (the contradiction dissolves) or converted to an instrument (the contradiction is real but unanswerable on desk evidence, so it becomes a trigger with a pre-defined response). None is "averaged."

[1] P12 SMALLNESS FORK — the plan's primary load-bearing trigger. Strongest version: the bridge wedge may be too narrow to fill 2+ senior calendars at premium prices; if so, the whole per-advisor model (D20), the premium (D17), and the capacity plan (R05) collapse together, because every motion now routes through the bridge wedge. Resolution — CONVERTED TO INSTRUMENT, fork stays OPEN by design. This is not reconcilable on desk evidence (T1/T2 are not desk-reachable). R09 D31-A made it a day-one instrument (qualified bridge-conversations/mo by channel + pipeline-to-core + the fork reading) with the response pre-defined: at Phase-1 exit (~month 9–12), if the trend tracks below 2-senior-calendar fill at premium realization → widen the wedge in a halo-preserving direction (adjacent regulated vendor-diligence triggers, inside the regulated/judgment identity, R04 D10/R07 §D) before dropping the premium; dropping premium is last resort. P11 confirms: per-advisor economics survive on demand/CAC/LTV (~7–20×) and break only on total qualified volume. Status: the single load-bearing Critical×Low trigger; carried to synthesis with instrument-and-fallback, NOT as a risk. Every other coherence condition above ultimately routes here.

[2] P5-vs-P9 owned-vs-borrowed origination MIX. Strongest version (P9): if owned content under-converts, the mix tilts permanently to partners and WNW becomes a pipeline tenant with no pricing power. (P5): if we over-invest in borrowed pipeline, we never build the owned demand that gives the firm independence and the premium. Resolution — RECONCILED IN PRINCIPLE, proportion instrumentation-decided. D27 (anti-tenancy conversion: every partner-originated land manufactures an owned reference + content artifact at scoping, published on the regulated axis) makes partners a feeder of owned demand, not a substitute — so the two aren't rivals, they're a pipeline-then-flywheel sequence. The realized proportion is decided by R09 D31-D: the borrowed→owned conversion rate per partner-originated land (anti-tenancy metric) + the content kill-criterion (R04#2 inbound-attributed pipeline + content-influenced win rate). If conversion lags, the firm is becoming a tenant and the content engine has failed its kill-criterion — both read on the same instrument. Status: reconciled in principle (D27); proportion = instrument (D31-D). Not a contradiction; a measured dial.

[3] P1-vs-P2 channel pace + regulated anchor. Resolution — RECONCILED (see §3, D34(b)). Resolved on frame-match (P10): the regulated anchor is fast vocabulary for the bridge buyer, slow only for the generic-SaaS buyer whom D10 excludes. P1's "anchor may suppress SaaS-fast access" warning stays an instrument (R07 D24(c)), gated T7. Status: reconciled by frame; residue instrumented.

[4] P3 founder-time veto + P11 capacity floor. Strongest version: a 2-person founding firm that runs a rich demand engine + a 30-metric dashboard spends the scarce senior hour on not-delivery; the plan dies of founder-time starvation before the wedge is even tested. Resolution — RECONCILED BY STRUCTURE. R09 made every milestone declare its senior-hour cost (D29), kept the Phase-1 metric set minimal (~a dozen) with full attribution deferred to the Phase-2 BD hire (D31), and built a standing founder-time-protection rule + monthly fused origination+capacity review + quarterly capacity-gate-with-a-real-veto (D32). The veto is on offered ladder rungs (R05 D16 capacity-sequencing) — the firm cannot commit scope its senior bench can't deliver at target utilization. Status: reconciled by structure (D29/D31/D32). The veto is real, not advisory.

[5] P7 Canada timing. Strongest version (P7): the freshest, least-crowded regulatory tailwind right now is Canadian (Streamlined Framework launched 25 Jun 2026, ~2 days ago); a long US-first deferral forfeits a first-mover window. (D6 counter): US-first wins on volume; Canada is differentiation-from-day-1 + second wave. Resolution — RECONCILED BY SEQUENCE, weight gated. D28 settled the structure: Canada (CCUA/CBA) presence is a month-1 milestone, NOT deferred behind US seals; the Streamlined-cohort second wave is a Phase-2 milestone gated T6 (Streamlined cohort velocity — partly desk-answerable, feeds R06). So Canada is present from day one (no first-mover forfeit on presence) but the weight of the early Canada bet rides on T6. Status: reconciled by sequence (D28); early-weight gated T6.

[6] The double-edged smallness (R03). Strongest version: the same narrowness that walls out the Big-4 ("too small to attack") could make the firm sub-scale ("too small to be a business"). Resolution — ROUTES TO THE FORK [1]. This is the sizing face of the smallness fork: "moat-or-sub-scale" is the same question as "does the wedge fill 2+ senior calendars." It is gated on T1/T2 (and R01's open buyer-adoption/ACV trigger). Status: not separately reconcilable; it IS trigger [1] seen from the moat side. Carried as the load-bearing fork.

P12 (closing the dissent walk): "Clean result. Four of the six reconcile by structure or frame and stop being contradictions. Two — the smallness fork and the owned/borrowed proportion — are real open questions, but neither is an internal incoherence: one is unanswerable on desk evidence (a signed trigger with a pre-defined pivot), the other is a dial we instrument and turn, not a fork in the plan. I am satisfied the reasoning is hardened. No dissent remains that fights another decision; the remaining openness is all external data we don't have yet."

> DECISION D35: DISSENT RECONCILIATION — the six carried dissents close as: [1] smallness fork = converted to the load-bearing instrument (open by design, pre-defined pivot); [2] owned/borrowed mix = reconciled in principle (D27), proportion instrumented (D31-D); [3] channel pace = reconciled by frame (D34(b)), residue instrumented (T7); [4] founder-time/capacity = reconciled by structure (D29/D31/D32, real veto); [5] Canada timing = reconciled by sequence (D28), early-weight gated T6; [6] double-edged smallness = the moat-side face of [1]. No dissent remains that contradicts another decision; all residual openness is external validation, not internal incoherence.

  3. Is the plan the strongest version of itself? Yes — conditionally, and the condition is honest: it is the strongest version of a bet on a narrow wedge. So the strongest-version verdict is: the internal logic is airtight and the external bet is named, instrumented, and pivot-ready. That is exactly what an integration round should deliver to a synthesis — not a guarantee, but a coherent plan whose single load-bearing uncertainty is measured on day one with the response decided in advance.

I have no remaining challenge that the room hasn't already absorbed into a decision or a trigger. The set is coherent. Proceed to synthesis."
